10-20 skilled human slaves: SZ M; AL varies; AC 10; MV 120’; HD 1-6 HP; HP 6, 6, 5(x4), 4(x4), 3(x4), 2(x4), 1, 1; #AT 1; Dmg by weapon.

3-6 skilled goblin slaves: SZ S; AL LE; AC 6; MV 60’; HD 1-1; HP 5, 4, 3, 3, 2, 2; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6.

### 4-13: Slave Pit: The Valuable

* Broadly similar, the third pit is a bit more luxurious than the first two.
	* Two ledges extend over the 25’-deep pit, each with a basket and winch.
	* The walls are painted in bright geometric patterns, and slope inwards and downward to a flat floor.
	* A 10’x10’ stone cistern stands under the northern ledge, filled with clean water.
	* A 2’-diameter latrine hole is on the western side of the floor, and extends down 10’.
	* The inmates have a decent supply of blankets, 2 spoons, and a pair of wooden buckets.
		* Hidden among the blankets is a shawl of warmth (new), which the inmates share among the most needy of their number.
	* The north door, at the end of the diagonal hallway, is iron and locked.
	* The south door is reinforced wood and is locked.
		* No guards are posted in front of it.

* The Guild consigns those it considers valuable to this pit.
	* Each week there is a 33% chance that 2-8 new inmates are added (max 30 pop).
	* At any time there are 10-19 valuable slaves in the pit.
	* They are well treated by the Guild, with extra food and better conditions. 
	* Despite favorable treatment, the classed characters are always plotting escape.
		* They have 2 small knives, a chisel, and 10’ of hand-made rope.
		* One of the current valuable slaves has concealed the fact that she is a cleric and is preparing her spells to aid her fellows in escape.
			* Captured alongside the Anchoress?  Or more recent?

d8 Reason for Value
* 1-2 Great beauty and/or physical attractiveness
* 3 Relative of a powerful figure
* 4-5 Expert skill (roll on table in area 4-12, but the slave has exceptional ability in this skill) 
* 6 Magic user or illusionist
* 7 Fighter, ranger or paladin
* 8 Thief or assassin

On north ledge, 2 guildsmen, as 2nd-level male Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 8; MV 120’; HD 2; HP 18, 15; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (spears, clubs). Possessions: leather armor; spears; and clubs. Special: they have +1 to damage from STR.

6-12 non-classed, valuable human slaves: SZ M; AL varies; AC 10; MV 120’; HD 1-6 HP; HP 6, 6, 5, 5, 4, 4, 3, 3, 2, 2, 1, 1; #AT 1; Dmg by weapon.

3-6 classed, valuable human or demi-human slaves: determine using NPC appendix.

Bergthora, 3rd-level female Wiskin cleric of Odin: SZ M; AL NG; AC 10; MV 120’; HD 3; HP 10 (max 18); #AT 1; Dmg by weapon. Abilities: STR 16, INT 14, WIS 17, DEX 10, CON 12, CHA 11. Spells: command, create water, resist cold, sanctuary; hold person(x2), silence 15’ radius. 

### 4-14: Chamber of Discipline

* This octagonal room is home to the main torture chamber of the Guild of Service.
	* It is brightly lit with continual light, with pale blue painted walls and ceiling.
	* Two adjustable wooden tables with leather restraints, and a shallow water pool with a sloped side (for water torture).
	* A tripod of heating (new) stands near the south wall.
	* 2 sets of manacles hang from the ceiling.
	* A rack of unpleasant instruments hangs on the northeast wall (250 gp to evil organizations).

* 50% chance that torture session is under way.
	* If so, the Chief Torturer, Ukamah Gol, is leading it, along with his two assistants.  Otherwise, the two assistants are present, lounging or sleeping.
* If confronted by obvious hostility, Ukamah Gol rushes to the doorway to 4-14a and shouts “Klimopercet! I require you!”, causing the demon Klimopercet manifests and joins the fray (see 4-14a).
	* The assistants do not know about the demon, but still do not enter 4-14a for any reason.

Ukamah Gol (50%), 7th-level male Khumus illusionist: SZ M; AL CE; AC 8; MV 120’; HD 7; HP 22; #AT 1; Dmg 1-4 (dagger). Abilities: STR 9, INT 16, WIS 11, DEX 16, CON 11, CHA 7. 
Special: infravision (120’); know alignment (1/day); detect lie (1/day); detect magic (1/day). 
* Possessions: dagger; ring of invisibility; pouch with 5 stones of striking (see new magic items); and a fist-sized piece of ivory carved as a human nose (the nose has been imbued with 2 charges of prismatic spray).
* Spells: change self, detect invisibility, light, wall of fog; brain full of small spiders (see new spells), deafness, improved phantasmal force; fear, paralyzation.
* Note: Ukamah Gol’s four special abilities are granted to him by the demon Klimopercet.

2 assistant torturers, 2nd-level male Thorcin fighters: SZ M; AL CE; AC 8; MV 120’; HD 2; HP 14, 13; #AT 1; Dmg 2-5 (dagger). Possessions: dagger; leather armor. Special: +1 to damage from STR.

##### 4-14a: Torturer’s Chamber

* Ukamah Gol, the Chief Torturer of the Guild of Service, makes his home in this narrow chamber.
	* Ukamah’s bed, a stool, a chest of clothing, an odd manikin, and countless handmade wooden, bone, and leather shelves of small size.
		* The area around the bed stinks of decay and blood, the floor under the bed is stained with copious amounts of spilled blood.
		* The mundane effects and clothing are ratty and unimpressive.
	* The shelves are packed with candles of all shapes and sizes; their flickering light lends the room a creepy aura. 
		* The candles (vaguely magical) are part of a charm to give protection to the torturer while he sleeps.
	* East wall (above the bed): covered with scrawling of various sizes and scripts, and in a variety of languages and inks.
		* If deciphered, each bit of writing in all languages says the same: “Klimopercet Requires Blood.”  The reader must save vs spells or be stunned 1d2 rounds from the blasphemous nature of the writing and its implications.
	* West wall (above door): Ukamah Gol has a surprising amount of wealth concealed in an invisible chest on an invisible shelf above the western door. 
		* 10 platinum bars (10 lb, 2,500 gp each), 4 lb of valuable spices (200 gp/lb), 4 golden teeth (10 gp each), potions (extra healing, growth), a scroll  (phantasmal force, deafness, rope trick, massmorph, tempus fugit), Ukamah Gol’s spell book. 

* Ukamah Gol is bound to a particularly nasty demon in a weird sort of reciprocal way.
	* The demon, Klimopercet, is bound to this chamber and requires near daily quantities of fresh blood to keep it from devouring Ukamah Gol.
	* The two have come to an uneasy agreement, with Ukamah Gol providing Klimopercet with blood, and Klimopercet providing Ukamah Gol with enhanced senses and attributes (and agreeing not to devour him).
	* The strain of this relationship has begun to tell on the torturer, who has begun to practice his trade regardless of its necessity.

* If anyone other than Ukamah Gol enters the chamber, the candles will gutter and flicker, and will start to extinguish themselves.
	* This takes 3d4 rounds. Once the last candle is extinguished, Klimopercet manifests, hungry for blood.  Relighting candles delays this, but they will keep going out.
	* Formally calling on Klimopercet to abjure this chamber banishes it for 1d3 days, but a sloppy adbjuration immediately extinguishes the candles and causes it to appear.
* If a hostile party encounters Ukamah Gol here, he swiftly invokes his demonic ally.

* Klimopercet can be distracted by significant (2 pints, or 5 hp) amounts of fresh blood.
	* Klimopercet understands Archontean, but can only communicate on this plane through a series of long keening tones that rise or fall after 5 seconds of stability (e.g., “Eeeeeeee-ah”).
	* Ukamah Gol doesn’t really understand this language, but knows how to placate the demon anyway.

Ukamah Gol (50%): for stats, see area 4-14.

Klimopercet, a blood-seeking demon (see new monsters): SZ M; AL CE; AC 0; MV 60’; HD 9; HP 61; #AT 3; Dmg 2-8/2-8/2-8; MR: 25%. Special attacks: drain blood; stun; darkness 2/
day. Special defenses: standard demonic defenses; toxic slime.
* Although Klimopercet could normally use gate to bring allies, the terms of his binding prevent him from using that so long as he is in 4-14 or 4-14a. 

Ukamah Gol’s Spell Book: Audible glamer, change self, chromatic orb, color spray, darkness, detect invisibility, light, phantasmal force, phantom armor, wall of fog; blur, brain full of small spiders (see new spells), deafness, detect magic, improved phantasmal force, invisibility, mirror image, misdirection; continual light, dispel illusion, fear, paralyzation; confusion, massmorph; shadow door.

### 4-15: Guard Post

* 3 guildsmen wait in this niche, on call in case of trouble in any of the three slave pits.
	* They are lazy and arrogant.
* They have several benches, a rickety table, playing cards, and a good stock of torches.

3 guildsmen, as 2nd-level male Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 8; MV 120’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 16; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (spears, clubs). Possessions: leather armor; spears; and clubs. Special: they have +1 to damage from STR.
* In the boot of one guildsmen, a golden fork (5 gp).

## Level 4: 16 - 30

### 4-16: Preparation

* This small chamber is where slaves destined for the auction block in 4-2 are prepared (mainly this means washing, primping, and dressing them).
	* The floor of the room slopes gently to a drain set in its center.
	* Wall-mounted basins are on the north and south walls; the fountainhead of each of basin is a rearing cobra, to which is attached a flexible, hide tube that can be used to drench the filthy slaves taken from the pits. 
* 25% chance a group of 8 slaves are being prepared here.  The preparation will involve four administrators from the guild and will be overseen by four bored (but well-armed) guildsmen.

8 slaves (25% chance): if indicated, roll d6: 1-3: unskilled slaves; 4-5: skilled; 6: valuable. Consult areas 4-11, 4-12, or 4-13 for the appropriate stats.

4 male Archontean administrators of the Guild of Service (25%): SZ M; AL LE; AC 10; MV 120’; HD 1-6 HP; HP 5, 3, 2, 2; #AT 1; Dmg 1-4 (dagger).

4 guildsmen, as 2nd-level male Archontean fighters (25% chance): SZ M; AL LE; AC 8; MV 120’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 16; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (spears, clubs). Possessions: leather armor; spears; and clubs. Special: they have +1 to damage from STR.

### 4-17: Plaza of the Guild

* This impressive square hall provides access between the Forum, the precincts of the Guild, and the Long Stair (4-19).
	* The roof  is 50’ above, sheathed in marble squares, and culminating in a roundel at the center of the arched roof. 
	* The north wall features several impressive, brightly-painted stone carvings.
		* 2 40' colossi of Set-animal-headed humans, carved in half-round, turned to the center of the wall, wielding whips.
			* Their eyes glitter in light, being pieces of amber (500 gp each).  Prying them out incurs a dreadful curse from Set himself (GM’s choice).
		* Between the figures, a smaller (20’-tall) naked human crouches, arms over his head for protection from the whips.
	* The plaza is lit with torches, and shares some of the light from the Forum.

* At all times the plaza is guarded by four well-armed guildsmen.
	* One holds the key to the locked door in 4-150.

4 guildsmen, as 2nd-level male Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 8; MV 120’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 16, 15; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (spears, clubs). Possessions: leather armor; spears; and clubs. 
Special: they have +1 to damage from STR.

### 4-18: Pit of the Damned

* This is the infamous fourth slave pit operated by the Guild of Service.
	* Here the Guild tosses those too weak to sell and/or proven too troublesome.
* The locked iron door leads to a twisting stone staircase that descends 40’ before opening into a dark landing.
	* Rising from the pit 40’ below is a foul reek of excrement and decay.
	* The pit contains 5-30 emaciated, starving, and cannibalistic wretches.
		* Most came from the Pit of the Laborers, but about 25% are adventurers (in a relatively healthy state).
	* An ancient stone cistern in the southwest corner contains a few inches of rancid water; the strongest inhabitants defend this resource ferociously.
		* Moisture from the walls will add 1” of liquid every week.
	* The floor of the pit is covered with a 3’-deep layer of bones, picked clean by the starving inmates, and a scattering of 23 sp and a large and beautiful beryl (500 gp).

5-30 poor souls of all races and types.

### 4-19: The Long Stair

* The Long Stair is well known in the Halls as a symbol of slavery and misery.
	* The stairs, carved from the bare rock, traverse 400’ in length and altitude, providing direct access to the precincts of the Guild of Service.
		* They are pitted and worn by the tread of countless feet. 
		* Every 30’ along the stairs is a carven face (twice human size, with realistic eyes, nose, and mouth) twisted into a rictus of agony or desperation, each unique.
			* The sound of desperate wailing and ululation can be heard by listening closely to the mouth of any face.
			* In one of the nostrils (cumulative 10% per face inspected) is a folded-up piece of parchment.
				* Instructions to a ‘great treasure’ within the halls (GM’s choice, but perhaps directions from the tomb of Marius (6-154) to the tomb of Lucius Cornelius scriptor (6-130 to 6-135)).
				* Also on the parchment are some cryptic notes: “Ekezalion,” “R3L2R7L2” and “Fear=Death.”
					* GM: gibberish, unless the GM wishes to assign meaning.
	* Secret Door (west, to 4-101a): opens by pushing a stone panel inwards.

### 4-20: Guild Members’ Recreation

* A chamber for the recreational perversions of the members of the Guild of Service.
	* The walls are cheaply whitewash with layers of graffiti, mostly pornographic and repulsive.
	* East wall: a wooden bar, where No-Thumbs serves tankards of Jobim’s lichen ale (1 sp/pint), and a huge hearth, lit by continual light (fuel is hard to come by).
	* Center: 10 round wooden tables with benches and chairs fill most of the center.
	* South wall: cloaked by a set of curtains, divided into 8’x8’ romance cubicles.
		* Unfortunate slaves provide ‘hospitality’ to guild members in these squalid and relatively public cubicles.
	* A number of off-duty guildsmen are always present, dicing, drinking, gambling, and generally relaxing.

1-3 male and 5-7 female Thorcin hospitality slaves: use stats for skilled slaves (see area 4-12). These slaves are handsome/pretty, and should be considered to have CHA 14-17.

3-8 guildsmen, as 2nd-level male Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 8; MV 120’; HD 2; HP 18, 17(x3), 16(x3), 15; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (spears, clubs). Possessions: leather armor; spears; and clubs. Special: they have +1 to damage from STR.

2-7 guildsmen, as 2nd-level male Archontean thieves: SZ M; AL LE; AC 6; MV 120’; HD 2; HP 10, 10, 9, 9, 8, 8, 7; #AT 1; Dmg 1-4 (dagger) or 1-6 (short sword). Thief skills: PP 35%, OL 34%, F/RT 25%, MS 21%, HS 15%, HN 10%, CW 86%. Possessions: leather armor; daggers; short swords. Special: they have DEX 16 on average.

No-Thumbs, 4th-level male Thorcin fighter and bartender: SZ M; AL NE; AC 10; MV 120’; HD 4; HP 27; #AT 1; Dmg 1-5 (club). Abilities: STR 15, INT 13, WIS 11, DEX 7, CON 11, CHA 9. Because he has no thumbs, the bartender is -2 to hit, and -1 to damage.

### 4-21: Inspection Point

* A heavily armed squad of Set guardsmen stands guard just north of the Darkness of Set (4-22), ready to inspect all seeking entrance to the Forum.
	* If the magic mouth at 4-22 is triggered, they are ready with spears and nets to greet all comers.
	* Those displaying a personalized travel pass or known personally to the sergeant can proceed immediately.  All others must submit to inspection and a 10 gp / person toll.
		* All persons must state their names, professions, and reasons for seeking entrance to the Forum.
		* Evasiveness or arrogance causes Sgt. Arethas to empty every pack and sack, while taking note of everything of value.
		* Those who are confident but humble can get away with a quick iteration of their personal possessions and of any trade goods they are carrying.
* The patrol members are dressed in red Set armor (av items) and each wears a set of magical eyes of Set (new).
	* Huge goggles with strange, greenish, crystalline lenses; somewhat intimidating (allows darkvision w/in darkness created by setite magic).
* Two benches and a locked wooden chest, along with a barrel of water.

Arethas, a Set sergeant (see new monsters), as a 5th-level Archontean fighter: SZ M; AL LE; AC 3; MV 60’; HD 5; HP36; #AT 1, Dmg 3-8 (mace +1), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: Set armor (av items) and wooden shield; footman’s mace +1; eyes of set (new), potion of healing, spear; light crossbow with 20 bolts.

6 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 17, 16, 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; eyes of set (new), footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts.

### 4-22: The Darkness of Set

* At the top of the Stair of Commerce (4-105) is an area of magical darkness (12th level to dispel), known as the Darkness of Set.
	* It covers the entire 20’x20’ area of the turn in the stairway, and can be seen from 75’ away due to the brightness of the rest of the stairs.
	* Hidden within the darkness is a cult statue of Set; most pass without ever knowing of its existence.
		* A magic mouth on the statue speaks (Mithric) when approaches within 10’ of the Darkness, “Set accepts the reverence of the humble. Approach as a supplicant, and be spared! Approach with hostility and be scourged!”
			* This almost always alerts the guards at 4-21.
		* An 8’-tall cult statue of Set in Set animal form.
			* If view, it is richly gilded and painted in classic pose, with citrine eyes (300 gp each), onyx ears (75 gp each), and ivory teeth (20x 25 gp each).
			* Attempts to despoil it cause a magic mouth (Archontean) “To me! Vandals! Thieves! To me!” and electric shocks (1d4 / round, 1 round to pry out one valuable item).
				* These cries draw immediate support from the guards at 4-21, whose  eyes of Set (new) can see in the darkness. 
* A 5’-square brass plaque is inset on the east wall just before the area of darkness.
	* Contains formal text (Mithric).  Preamble: "Visitors to the Forum shall advance five paces, turn to the right, and advance another five paces before submitting to inspection. Hostile actions will be met with a swift and severe response. Death, loss, or servitude is the just fate of all who trifle with Lord Set or neglect to adhere to his most reasonable laws."  A list of The Laws of the Forum (see 4-2) follows.

### 4-23: 1st Mystery of Set: the Black Boar

* This hall houses the first of the three Mysteries of Set, that of the Black Boar.
	* The hall is 25’ tall and sheathed in panels of black marble.
	* Two 10’x10’ niches in the western wall are pens fenced with iron bars.
		* Each holds an enormous wild boar who slavers, grunts, and foams the entire time visitors are present.
		* If visitors prove hostile or unduly disrespectful, a Set acolyte will emerge from the Boar and release the boars, who will attack anyone and everyone in sight or scent range.
		* Amid the dirty straw of one pen is a torn fragment of a treasure map.
	* At the east end, 15' up on either side of the entrance, is a semi-circular balcony.
		* Narrow tunnels lead from the balconies to 4-2F.
		* On each ledge, 2 Set guardsmen with crossbows, wearing eyes of Set (new), stand during the mystery ceremony.  If combat breaks out, one of the four will rush to alert the Forum while the other three fire bolts.
	* The Boar sits on an 8’-tall rectangular slab of granite.
		* It is 8’ long, 5’ wide, and 8’ tall; cleverly constructed of wood, wire, and plaster, with large ivory tusks (245 gp each).  It is painted a matte black, with numerous bits of colored glass and fragments of bone embedded in its surface.
		* The boar is partly magical and partly mechanical.  It uses magic mouths to speak the ritual.  Two Set acolytes are responsible for operating the boar from a cramped chamber within during performance of the mystery.  They pull levers, activate smoke and magical effects, creating a dramatic, if slightly cheesy, display.
	* Secret Door (west): difficult to detect (1 in 8) and unknown to the cult of Set.
		* It opens by rapping 5 times in rapid succession on the door itself.

The First Mystery
* The first mystery is open to all, and newcomers to the Forum will frequently be urged to visit it.  This chamber is one of the most commonly visited within the precincts of Set.
	* The mystery occurs every hour on the hour. Visitors begin gathering 15 minutes early under the overhang of the Porch of Scrutiny (4-2F).  2 lazy guardsmen with polearms stand in front of the door to 4-23, preventing entry until appropriate.
* This mystery recreates one of the legendary stories of Set.
	* When the other gods began to cavil at his forceful deeds and to levy restrictions on his actions, Set sought a way to operate outside of their prying gaze.
	* Changing into one of his favorite forms, a colossal black boar, Set leaped forth and swallowed the sun, thus preventing the others from seeing his form or his deeds and, incidentally, plunging the world into chaos.
	* Only after the other gods agreed to cease interfering with his affairs did the Set boar belch forth the sun. 
* The Mystery of the Black Boar
	* At the stroke of the hour, the guardsmen open the door to 4-23 and visitors crowd into the chamber. The guards then shut the doors, and the celebrants are left in darkness, save for a dull globe of yellow light bobbings above their heads.
	* At five minutes past the hour a disembodied voice, nasal and reedy, proclaims slowly in Archontean, “The Sun God lorded over the lands, confident in his power and his distance from earth.”  The globe of light glows oppressively bright.
	* Three minutes later, a deep, charismatic new voice proclaims “But Lord Set disdains arrogance without strength. And so he assumed his favored form and Lo! (a rumble of drums and a crash of cymbals), Lord Set devoured the Sun God!”  Bright light fills the rest of the chamber, revealing the boar.
		* First-time visitors usually gasp to see a huge black boar standing on an 8’-tall platform in front of them.
	* The boar lunges forward and upward and devours the orb of light, plunging the room back into darkness, filled with terrible sounds of rending, groaning and grinding.  A faint outline of the boar, illuminated in red light can be seen, towering over the celebrants.
	* The stentorian voice ends the ritual in these words “The arrogant and foolish Sun God was held in darkness, until the gods submitted.  Thus Lord Set's might triumphs over all!”  The celebrants kneel before the boar.
		* Celebrants who kneel receive a blessing for 1 week: +1 morale, +1 loyalty to their master, and -2 to saves against spells from Set's priests.
	* The doors open, and visitors are ushered back into the Forum, usually to mill about for a bit.

2 Set acolytes (see new monsters), as 3rd-level Archontean clerics of Set: SZ M; AL LE; AC 4; MV 60’; HD 3; HP 19, 17; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (mace) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Possessions: Set 
armor (see Arden Vul items); footman’s mace; light crossbow; acolyte’s was stick (see new magic items); and a silver holy symbol of Set (10 gp). Spells prayed for: command, cure light 
wounds, curse (reverse of bless), protection from good; hold person, silence 15’ radius.

4 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts.

2 enormous wild boars: SZ M; AL N; AC 7; MV 150’; HD 4+3; HP 29, 27; #AT 1; Dmg 3-12. Special attacks: fights for 2-5 rounds after 0 HP reached, or until -7 HP is reached.

##### 4-23a: Portcullis

* A floor-to-ceiling iron portcullis blocks the passage here, with a 3’x8’ door is embedded in the framework (locked, keys held only by select priests).

### 4-24: Vaults of Set

* The door to the vaults is iron, with three locks (Difficult, -10% to pick).
	* Different persons hold the keys to the locks: Helena of Archontos (4-2G), the current Duty Deacon (4-2), and the trio of Forum Inspectors (4-2).
* The 15’-tall vault is lined with lead from floor to ceiling (blocks teleportation and scrying).
	* On the east wall, next to the door, is a ‘statue’ of a boar-headed human in a kilt, with spear and club.
		* It is an Archontean animated construct – bipedal boar (new), attacks any who do not display one of the three vault keys.
	* Stacks of crates, sacks, kegs, and iron lock-boxes fill the chamber. A few large art objects are also stored here.
		* About 30 wooden crates (avg 3’ x 4’ x 2’) are stacked in the central area.
			* Typically hold bulk items like apples, salted pork, dried meat, raw spices, dried mushrooms, charcoal and other carbon sources, iron ingots, etc.
			* About 3/4 have already been purchased by the cult of Set for its own uses.
		* About 50 sacks, in 5-, 10-, or 20-lb varieties) hold fresh vegetables, fruits, flour, cornmeal, and salt.
			* Most have already been purchased by the cult of Set from merchants.
		* A huge, 120-gallon barrel of ale with 10 standard (30-gallon) barrels of beer, ale, and mead (100 gp each), as well as twelve 5-gallon casks of brandy (100 gp each) stacked around it.
			* All of these liquors have been purchased by the cult of Set.
		* About a dozen pieces of large potentially valuable objects are at the west end (see below).
		* 30 iron lockboxes line a set of open shelves along the north wall.
			* Twenty of the boxes are 3’ long, 2’ wide, and 1’ tall; ten more are 6’ long, 3’ wide and 2’ tall.
				* The traders and others who need to store substantial wealth rent these lockboxes from Helena of Archontos (4-2G).
				* Currently ten of the smaller and two of the larger boxes are in use; the others have their keys in the locks. (see below).
		* Three enormous stone chests (5’ x 5’ x 5’) with complex, poison-trapped locks sit against the east wall.
			* These chests contain the liquid wealth that the Set cult (mostly) uses to purchase goods and pay its guardsmen, informers, and spies.
			* Keys are held by Stephania (4-51), Helena of Archontos (4-2G), Gunnar (4-10), and Belisarius (4-47).
			* Chest #1: 36,712 cp stacked in neat columns; a bolt of purple silk embroidered with elephants (225 gp)
			* Chest #2: 11,578 sp; 3,456 ancient silver pennies; 6,789 gp
			* Chest #3: 726 aquamarines worth 100 gp each; two 5-lb cones of sugar (66 gp each); four 10-lb ingots of platinum (2,500 gp each)

### 4-25: Traders’ Square and Well

* This arched chamber is 20’ tall and brightly lit with continual light.
	* There are numerous stone benches and a 100’-deep well filled with slightly musty but potable water.
	* Spy holes are cleverly concealed in the stonework of the north wall, for those in 4-36 to observe activities here.
	* Any inhabitants of 4-26 through 4-35 might be encountered here. 

### 4-26: Hazlitt One-Eye (see 4-2d)

* This large chamber contains a large feather bed, an extra-large iron lock-box, an armoire, a chamber pot, a leather stuffed chair, and a wooden desk and chair.
	* Hazlitt has added a fine oriental-style carpet (140 gp), a shelf holding two primitive telescopes (100 gp each), and a bust of himself in marble (20 gp).
	* Hazlittt keeps his best items in his large lockbox at 4-24.
	* Several spy holes are cleverly concealed in the stonework of the north wall; the holes allow those in 4-36 to observe all activities in this area.

Hazlitt One-Eye: for stats, see 4-2d.

### 4-27: Helena of Archontos

* This chamber has the same basic furnishings as Hazlitt’s (4-26).
	* Helena has added a pair of comfortable leather armchairs, a wooden screen painted with scenes of the tales of Larel One-Eye, and a tapestry showing the 5th labor of Arden (see SL13-10e).
		* Helena has a humidor filled with mildly narcotic ‘tobacco’.
	* Desk
		* Top: jade inkwell (55 gp), ivory blotter (60 gp), sheaf of fine parchment (2 gp).
		* Locked drawer: book of accounts for the cult of Set for the past month (500 gp to the Drome).
	* A battered urn made of copper (actually tarnished gold, 155 gp) with a scene from the 3rd labor of Arden embossed on one side (see SL13-10c) sits by the door, filled with six carved walking sticks.
		* Hidden inside the urn is a pouch filled with gold dust (245 gp).
	* Several spy holes are cleverly concealed in the stonework of the north wall; the holes allow those in 4-36 to observe all activities in this area.

Helena of Archontos: for stats, see 4-2g.

### 4-28: Robben the Fat (see 4-2d)

* This small chamber contains a normal bed, an armoire, a writing table, and a basic chair.
	* Robben has a humidor and a pile of hides and skins on which he ‘entertains’ his female visitors.
		* Robben keeps a stash of gold coins (55 gp) buried in his mattress.
	* The rest of the room is filthy and cluttered with bits of food and loose clothing.

Robben the Fat: for stats, see 4-2d.

1 female Thorcin pleasure slave (50% chance): SZ M; AL N; AC 10; MV 120’; HD 1-6 HP; HP 2; #AT 1; Dmg by weapon.

### 4-29: Horace Trych (see 4-2d)

* The basic furnishings are identical to those found in 4-28.
	* A banner of the Great Boar of Set adorns the wall above the bed (part of his cover).
	* A beautiful polar-bear fleece (450 gp) rug and a marble bust of Licinus Bonus Apsus, one of the ancient claustral priors of the cult of Thoth (a head of Thoth, new).
		* Horace knows the bust is magic, but not what it does.
	* The desk contains a (fake) diary that Horace maintains scrupulously.
		* It holds Horace’s portrayal of a stereotypically evil person, full of derisory accounts of weaklings, the need to exert power over others, and a philosophy of lawful obedience to power, no matter what that power chooses to do. 
			* Exposed as a phony if a LE aligned person reads it more than a day.
	* A permanently invisible, lead casket is affixed to the ceiling above the bed.
		* It holds 25 pp, an amulet of life protection, a holy symbol of the immortal flame, and Horace's true diary.

Horace Trych: for stats, see area 4-2D.
* Most of Horace’s wealth is stored at 4-24

### 4-30: Servants’ Dormitory

* In the old days, traders were often accompanied by numerous servants, and this 20’x30’ room was designated for their use.
	* Plain stone, outfitted with eight rickety wooden bunk beds, several sets of wooden pegs set into the walls, and two large wooden chests (lacking locks).
	* Two battered pitchers stand on an equally battered wooden table near the door
		* One of the pitchers smells strongly of urine.
* Currently only one bed is occupied, by Asbjorn, servant of Birgir (4-2D).
	* Asbjorn is Birgir’s cousin and resents being treated as a servant.
	* He possesses two sets of nice clothing, and a pouch of filched gemstones hidden under his mattress (2d6 stones worth 10d10 each).
	* Due to his discontent and loneliness, Asbjorn is willing to listen to offers from those who cultivate his friendship.

Asbjorn: for stats, see 4-2D.

## Level 4: 31 - 45

### 4-31: Galadnor Half-Elven (see 4-2d)

* The basic furnishings are the same as those found in 4-28.
	* A bronze tripod of heating (new) for light and heat.
	* 3 large wall tapestries depicting pastoral scenes, and woven reed mats dyed a pleasant purple color.
	* Underneath the bed is a small, locked wooden chest, with a poison needle trap.
		* Inside is Galadnor’s spell book; a pouch with 149 gp; a lump of raw jade (110 gp), a fist-sized lump of raw arcanum carefully wrapped in felt (new), and scrolls (power word stun, irresistible dance, planar punishment (new)).
	* Affixed to the underside of the desk is a small pouch.
		* Incriminating documents that reveal Marius Junienos’s (4-56) addiction to a psychotropic drug (worth 250 gp to High Priestess Stephania at 4-51).
	* The magic items she has available for sale are found in her lockbox at 4-24.

Galadnor Half-Elven: for stats see 4-2d.

Galadnor’s Spell Book: Alarm, burning hands, charm person, comprehend languages, detect magic, enlarge, identify, light, magic missile, read magic, shield, ventriloquism, write; detect good, forget, knock, locate object, mirror image, strength, wizard lock; clairvoyance, phantasmal force, protection from normal missiles, slow, suggestion, tiny hut, tongues.

### 4-32: Birgir the Gem-Trader (see 4-2d)

* The room features the same basic furnishings as 4-28, plus a hammock.
	* A large potted palm tree from which hang bits of string, colored glass, and a pair of metal gauntlets. 
		* Birgir keeps his big gems buried in the palm-tree pot: two 500 gp peridots, one 1,500 gp fire-yellow topaz, and six 250 gp corals of unusual size.
		* Hidden in the dirt are five rot grubs; while ‘gardening’, Birgir uses gauntlets to avoid the grubs.
	* Birgir does not trust the security of the Vault of Set and has his own lockbox (2’x1’x1’) hidden under his bed.
		* Contains: brightly colored, loose clothing, a jeweler’s loupe and other tools, a fine mancala set with moonstones for stones (225 gp); 5 aquamarines (100 gp each), and fifteen azurite gems (10 gp each).

5 rot grubs: SZ S; AC 9; MV 10’; HD 1 HP; HP 1, 1, 1, 1, 1; #AT 0; Dmg nil. Special attacks: burrow into flesh, and kill in 1-3 turns.

Birgir: for stats, see area 4-2D.

### 4-33: Skellan Skindros (see 4-2d)

* The chamber boasts the same basic furnishings as 4-28.
	* A simple alchemical apparatus is set up on the desk.
		* Ingredients for potions and poisons in the drawer, along with 3 powerful poisons and potions of hill giant strength, levitation, and sweet water.
	* A wooden wine-rack with space for 24 bottles.
		* 14 bottles of foul home-brewed wine (1 gp each), 6 bottles of fine brandy (50 gp each), 4 bottles of superior wine (75 gp).

Skellan Skindros: for stats, see 4-2D.

### 4-34: Currently Uninhabited Chamber

* Same basic furnishings as 4-28.

### 4-35: Currently Uninhabited Chamber

Same basic furnishings as 4-28.

### 4-36: Forgotten Spy Tunnels

* These narrow corridors allowed ancient spymasters of Set to spy on the trader’s square.
	* Unused for centuries, the tunnels are cold, dark, and extremely dusty (2”-thick layer).
	* Spy-holes provide clear viewing of activities in 4-25, 4-26 and 4-27.
	* Access to the tunnels and the spymasters’ lair (4-37 to 4-39) is via secret doors to 4-23 and to the corridor connecting 4-61 to 4-48.
		* Secret Door (north): small (4’ x 2.5’), easy to locate from this side (1 in 4 chance). Opens by knocking four times in rapid succession on the door.
		* Secret Door (east): easy to locate from this side (1 in 4 chance). Opens by knocking five times on the door itself. 

### 4-37: Forgotten Chamber

* This former planning chamber was the seat of the original Set cult’s considerable spy networks during the glory days of Arden Vul.
	* Two wooden frames occupy the western wall; each with parchment maps pinned up.
	* A 10' square wooden table occupies the center, around which are several benches.
		* Several candelabra rest on the table, along with 1d8 more maps, plus 1d4 writs and a few blank sheets of parchment.
			* The maps are of great potential value.
				* The GM should decide in advance which areas they represent.  Each contains good information on ~20 rooms from Levels 1-5.  Certain areas should be off limits (e.g., the midnight road), but the rest should be fair game as a reward to a party locates this hoard.
	* A cabinet against the south wall has four shelves filled with a variety of useful things for a spymaster
		* Small boxes containing wooden counters of different colors and shapes; a supply of parchment, quills, and ink (dry); 100 carnelians of low quality (10 gp each); several sticks of sealing wax plus some fragments of sticks; a variety of stolen signet rings (worth 10d10 gp each), etc.
	* The east wall has a row of wooden pegs, one holding a battered cloak. 

### 4-38: Long Dead Spymaster

* Here lived the spymaster for the old cult of Set.
	* When the end of the city was nigh, the last master, Constantius Silvius, chose to seal his secrets away and commit suicide rather than allow generations of intelligence to be pillaged by forces unknown.
* Constantius’s chambers are relatively spartan.
	* A large and somewhat unsettling portrait of the spy-lord stares from the south wall.
		* This portrait depicts a gaunt man in white-face with red cheek-spots, a pronounced Roman nose, several warts on his forehead, and piercing eyes suggestive of cold intelligence.
	* A now-crumbling four-poster bed, an easy chair, a writing desk, a scroll case, a water barrel (now dry), a chest, and a small table with a platinum dining service. 
		* Platinum dining service (3 goblets, ewer, plate, silverware, serving bowl, 800 gp)
			* The goblet in Constantius’s hands is still coated with poison.
		* Scroll case: 3-12 scrolls with incriminating (but out-of-date) information about imperial officials and families.
			* Historical value to an imperial collector, and could plant a seed for a quest involving current political factions.
		* Chest: faded but usable Set ceremonial robes (100 gp to current Setites).
* Sitting in the chair of the writing desk is a desiccated corpse that still grips one of the platinum goblets.
	* This is Constantius, who drank hemlock and died as the city fell into chaos. 
	* His last testament lies before him.
		* It is strangely personal and emotional, with numerous underlined words and strangely capitalized letters (as if it were a 19th-century romantic novel).
		* The writing is breathless, a lament over the decline and fall of Arden Vul, the futility of his life, and his regrets at tasks left unaccomplished.
		* It contains nothing useful because it is, in fact, a simple code: the underlining indicates a space in the message (i.e., it should not be read), while the capitalized letters, if removed and unscrambled, reveal a message.
			* 4d8 under INT to detect the secret (secret tongue of the priests of Set): “To my successor: Seek the documents in the room opposite. They are revealed by invoking the Black Boar. Speak Thrice Five.“

### 4-39: Lesser Conference Room

* This chamber is similarly furnished to 4-37, save the absence of maps and documents.
	* An invisible chest is hidden under the middle of the conference table.
		* Speaking (Mithric) "black boar" reveals the chest beneath the table (one must still look beneath the table to see it).
		* The grey plasteel chest, a rudishva relic, has a clear panel on its front.
			* It opens by speaking the number 5 three times in a row (‘thrice five’) in Mithric or Rudishva.
			* 12x 10-lb bars of pure platinum (2,500 gp each) and extremely sensitive documents involving the imperial family.
				* Although over one thousand years old, they still possess volatile political value (at the GM’s wish: they might reveal that the imperial family is descended from bastards, or that they worship demons, or something like that).
	* The corpses of two murdered servants of Constantius are slumped in the room.
		* One has risen as a wraith.
	* Secret Door (west): opens by pushing the corner of one of the map frames.
		* It leads to a tiny chamber with a series of rough-carved, cutback stairs descending 60’ to a short tunnel to the Shrine of the Snake (4-51a).
		* The secret door is of recent construction (see 4-51a, made by the Kaliyani).

1 wraith: SZ M; AL LE; AC 4; MV 120’, 240’ flying (Class B); HD 5+3; HP 37; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: energy drain. Special defenses: silver or magic weapons to hit; immune to sleep, charm, hold, cold, poison, and paralysis.

### 4-40: Guard Barracks: Alpha Sept

* This barracks is the home of the elite company of Set guardsmen.
	* 40 guardsmen reside here, only 8 present at any given time.
		* 50% chance Sergeant Theodora, the sept leader, is present.
	* Alpha Sept uses the black boar as its chief symbol; this image is painted in vivid red and black on the wooden door to their barracks.
* The barracks chamber is 20’ tall and is painted in bright yellow paint.
	* The center and east end are filled with a maze of eighteen wooden triple bunk beds (space for 54 persons).
		* Forty simple wooden lockers are pushed under the bunkbeds, each containing personal items and 2-12 sp of small valuables. 
	* The western end of the room is relatively open, containing several weapon and armor racks, a large barrel of water, and a long trestle table with benches, bronze cups, and several containers of water, mushroom ale, and lichen ale.
		* The triangular war-pennon of the sept hangs on the western wall.
		* The sept’s war chest is under the table.
			* 2,931 sp and 12,641 cp for use in emergencies by members of the sept.
	* The sept keeps a large billy goat named Sparky as a mascot.
		* Sparky has the run of the barracks, and is quite aggressive. The lowest ranking member of the sept has the unenviable task of cleaning up after Sparky.

8 elite Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 3rd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 3; HP 26, 26, 25(x3), 24(x3); #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts.

Sergeant Theodora (50% chance), the Set sergeant (see new monsters), as a 5th-level female Archontean fighter: SZ M; AL LE; AC 3; MV 60’; HD 5; HP 40; #AT 1, Dmg 3-8 (mace +1), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: Set armor (see Arden Vul items) and wooden shield; footman’s mace +1; spear; light crossbow with 20 bolts.

Sparky, goat: SZ M; AL N; AC 7, MV 150’; HD 1+2; HP 7; #AT 1; Dmg 1-3. Special attacks: charge.

### 4-41: Storeroom and Cook

* This small chamber is filled with shelves containing cookware, spices, root vegetables, dried fruit, and nuts.
	* Cot and personal effects of Gresta, the ancient cook.
	* 25% chance Gresta is here, otherwise in 4-42.

Gresta, female human noncombatant (25%): AC 10, HP 2.
* Gresta wears a badly corroded bracelet that appears to be iron, but is in fact platinum washed with iron (125 gp).
 
### 4-42: Kitchen

* The main kitchen of the Set compound is a busy place, with guardsmen and acolytes constantly circulating through for a quick meal.
	* A hearth in the southwest corner has several enchanted heat-stones over which the cook (Gresta) prepares her meals, usually nourishing but bland "cavern stew".  Sometimes she roasts meat or prepares a special dessert.
	* A preparation table and six trestle tables with benches.
		* Gresta’s helper, the goblin Rocko, sleeps under the prep table. Rocko knows of the escaped slaves to the north (4-100) and has contemplated joining them.
	* Two huge barrels of water line the western wall.

Gresta, female human noncombatant (75%): AC 10, HP 2.

Rocko, goblin sous-chef: SZ S; AL LE; AC 6; MV 60’; HD 1-1; HP 4; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6.

1-2 Set acolytes (see new monsters), as 3rd-level Archontean clerics of Set: SZ M; AL LE; AC 4; MV 60’; HD 3; HP 19, 18; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (mace) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Possessions: Set armor (see Arden Vul items); footman’s mace; light crossbow; acolyte’s was stick (see new magic items); and a silver holy symbol of Set (10 gp). Spells prayed for: command, cure light wounds, curse (reverse of bless), protection from good; hold person, silence 15’ radius.

0-1 Set deacons (see new monsters), as a 6th-level Archontean cleric of Set: SZ M; AL LE; AC 3; MV 90’; HD 6; HP 39; #AT 1; Dmg 3-8 (mace +1). Possessions: Set armor +1 (see Arden Vul items); deacon’s was stick (see new magic items); footman’s mace +1; an amulet of protection against normal missiles (see new magic items); a potion of extra healing; a potion of glibness; a scroll of knit bones (see new spells); and a gold holy symbol of Set (150 gp). Spells prayed for: command, cure light wounds (x2), cause fear, protection from good; chant, hold person, know alignment, resist fire, silence 15’ radius; animate dead, dispel magic, cause blindness; cause serious wounds.

3-8 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 17, 16, 16, 15, 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 
(light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts.

### 4-43: Inner Plaza and Set Triumphant

* This large room features a pretty, 20’-tall vaulted ceiling painted sky blue, with a continual light spell in its center provides light. 
	* Facing the Long Stair (4-19) from the center of the chamber is another 15' tall cult statue of Set, in human form.
		* The statue is black basalt, brightly painted, with purple robes, a white face, green eyes, black eyelids, and flaming red hair.  It is posed as a confident ruler, cradling an ankh and a rod of authority in his elbows.
* This plaza is a favored gathering place for the lesser acolytes of the cult.
	* There are always 4-7 acolytes in several knots, whispering, pointing at other groups, and gossiping among themselves.
	* 20% chance an important personage is also present.
		* The overseer (4-47), the master of the Guild of Service (4-10), or one of the upper priesthood (4-51, 4-56, or 4-57).

1 Set acolyte (see new monsters), as a 3rd-level Archontean cleric of Set: SZ M; AL LE; AC 4; MV 60’; HD 3; HP 19; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (mace) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Possessions: Set 
armor (see Arden Vul items); footman’s mace; light crossbow; acolyte’s was stick (see new magic items); and a silver holy symbol of Set (10 gp). Spells prayed for: command, cure light 
wounds, curse (reverse of bless), protection from good; hold person, silence 15’ radius.

Important personage (20%). See above.

### 4-44: Guard Barracks: Beta Sept

This barracks is the home of the second company of Set guardsmen.
* 40 guardsmen reside here, only 8 present at any given time.
	* 50% chance Sergeant Justinus, the sept leader, is present.
	* Beta Sept uses an image of a stylized head with bone white face and red hair as its symbol.  This image is painted on the east wall opposite the entrance to the barracks.
* The barracks chamber is 20’ tall and its entrance is covered with a leather curtain.
	* The center and east end are filled with a maze of eighteen wooden triple bunk beds (space for 54 persons).
		* Forty simple wooden lockers are pushed under the bunkbeds, each containing personal items and 2-12 sp of small valuables. 
	* The western end of the room is relatively open, containing several weapon and armor racks, a large barrel of water, and a long trestle table with benches, bronze cups, and several containers of water, mushroom ale, and lichen ale.
		* The circular war-pennon of the sept hangs on the south wall.
		* The sept’s war chest is under the table.
			* 1,799 sp and 8,941 cp for use in emergencies by members of the sept.

Sergeant Justinus (50%), the Set sergeant (see new monsters), as a 5th-level Archontean fighter: SZ M; AL LE; AC 3; MV 60’; HD 5; HP 41; #AT 1, Dmg 3-8 (mace +1), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: Set armor (see Arden Vul items) and wooden shield; footman’s mace +1; spear; light crossbow with 20 bolts.

4 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 17, 16, 16, 15, 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 
(light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts.

### 4-45: Inspection Point

* A pair of guardsmen watch the iron bars blocking access to the northern caves.
	* The guardsmen are usually bored, without good light- or noise-discipline.
	* The iron gate has a locked, man-sized door.
		* Keys are given to patrol leaders venturing out, and one is kept by the corporal of this inspection point.
		* They won't admit unauthorized visitors without first summoning a more important figure, such as the Overseer (4-47).
		* They furiously ring a gong on the wall if threatened.
	* A bench and small table for endless hands of cards.
	* On the north wall is the partner to the magic mouth of 4-84.
		* If intruders are spotted there, the guards here are alerted, and a patrol from 4-46 is sent out to investigate. 

2 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts.

## Level 4: 46 - 60

* This barracks is the home of the third company of Set guardsmen.
	* 40 guardsmen reside here, only 8 present at any given time.
		* 50% chance Sergeant Heraclion, the sept leader, is present.
	* Gamma Sept calls itself the Company of the Desert Storm, and uses a tornado as its symbol. The tornado is worked into a set of hanging beads that blocks the entrance to the barracks, and is painted in black on the yellow walls of the barracks proper. 
* The barracks chamber is 20’ tall and is painted in bright yellow paint.
	* The center and east end are filled with a maze of eighteen wooden triple bunk beds (space for 54 persons).
		* Forty simple wooden lockers are pushed under the bunkbeds, each containing personal items and 2-12 sp of small valuables. 
	* The western end of the room is relatively open, containing several weapon and armor racks, a large barrel of water, and a long trestle table with benches, bronze cups, and several containers of water, mushroom ale, and lichen ale.
		* The rectangular war-pennon of the sept hangs on the south wall.
		* The sept’s war chest is under the table.
			* 1,331 sp and 9,834 cp for use in emergencies by members of the sept.

 8 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 16, 16, 15, 15, 14, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4
