### 4-85: Hidden Preparation Room

* Accessible only from the river or the secret door in 4-86, this forgotten chamber was used during the Archontean golden age by sorcerers wishing to prepare for a safe - but rapid - descent through the waters of Level 4 and 5.
* The chamber worked-stone walls were once painted, but now coated merely with smears of mildewed color.
	* The slick floor has been paved with slate flagstones.
	* A great roaring sound comes from river, especially from the area to the east (4-65). 
	* A 6’-diameter ring of mosaic tiles showing piscine scenes is inlaid on the floor near the western wall.
		* Nestled among the fish is the inscription (in Mithric): ‘What do you require?’
		* Speaking the command phrase (Mithric) “I require transport” causes a new ‘egg’ to appears magically on the mosaic.
	* Against the north wall rest two egg-shaped vessels some 8’ tall and 6’ wide.
		* They appear made of leather or hide and both feature a 4’-square flap. 
		* One egg has two loose ancient octagonal platinum coins.
		* Inside each egg, three seats attached to the walls and a small metal cube is attached to the ‘floor’, with a fish-shaped indentation on top.
* 3 medium creatures can squeeze into an eggs and be launched into the river.
	* Without a stabilizing control rod inserted into the fish-shaped indentation on the cube, this will likely prove fatal as the occupants are thrown about as the egg plummets down the chute (4-65) and into the river on Level 5.
	* With a control rod, the egg remains perfectly stable despite the roughness of its passage.
	* The remaining control rods are at 3-67, 4-2d, 5-102, 7-76c, 8-146, 9-33, and SL4-40f.  Kerbog Khan also has a number of control rods in his possession at any given time (see SL12-23).

### 4-86: Quiet Cave

* Some long-dead sorcerers have enchanted this small natural cave to be inimical to monsters. One can safely rest here.
* Secret Door (south): perfectly camouflaged with the cave wall and difficult to find (1 in 8).
	* It's hidden catch is then easy to find and pull.

### 4-87: Descending Tunnel to 5-33

* This cold and drafty tunnel descends 100’ to 5-33.

### 4-88: Ascending Tunnel to Level 3 (3-115)

* This rocky tunnel climbs 100’ to debouche in 3-115.
	* A light breeze runs upwards in the direction of 3-115.

### 4-89: Golden Monkey

* This large cavern is moist, cool, and empty.
	* A strange, solid gold, statuette of a monkey (2000 gp) was abandoned by an adventurer on a ledge in the southwestern corner.
		* The monkey has four sets of limbs: legs in the lotus position, while three sets of arms cover its ears, eyes, and mouth respectively.
		* A huge single eye, inset with lapis lazuli, is set in its rotund belly.
		* Its base is inscribed (Mithric) “Victory!”.
		* The monkey is cursed (detects of magic and chaos): the first to pick it up goes deaf, dumb and blind unless covering the eye on its belly when picking it up.

### 4-90: Crystalline Growths and Tunnel Down to 7-118

* Colossal columns of gypsum crisscross the chamber.
	* The temperature here is quite hot (~120F) and the humidity is close to 100%.
	* Embedded amid the growths is a brightly lit silver bell some 3’ in diameter (400 lbs, 400 gp, continual light enchantment).
* Four selenite guardians tend the cave, and will be upset if intruders disturb the gypsum (e.g. to recover the bell).
	* They will remonstrate in their own language, but attack if unable to communicate.
* The tunnel to the west leads downward 900’ to 7-118.

4 selenite guardians (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 2; MV 30’ on dirt, 60’ on selenite; HD 6; HP 41, 37, 36, 35; #AT 2; Dmg 2-8/2-8. Special defenses: regenerate 2 HP/round near 
selenite; immune to fire and water; take only 1 HP from edged weapons.

## Level 4: 91 - 100

### 4-91: Swift Stream

* The 3' deep stream flows south at a swift pace through a 6'-tall tunnel.
	* It is possible to wade upstream (3d8 under DEX or slip and be swept downstream for 2d6 damage).
	* A bolt of fire (new) is jammed in a cleft where the stream crosses above 4-73.

### 4-92: Crossroads

* Four distinct tunnels converge in this crossroads cave.
	* The floor is rocky and uneven, but subtle tracks lead northwest.
	* A faint smell of cooking meat comes from the same direction.

### 4-93: Side Cave

* The cave is empty save for three rotting - and gutted - lizard carcasses.
	* Hoping to trap some subterranean lizards or other edible prey, the escaped slaves (4-100) have rigged a rock fall over the entrance to this cave (2d6 damage).
		* Within 2 turns, a group of 5 slaves arrives to investigate the noise.

### 4-94: Misty Cave

* This damp and misty cave drops 20’ from the main tunnel.
	* Visibility is only 10’ in the mist.
	* At the cave entrance is a petrified Set guardsman, caught trying to cover his eyes.
		* Despite the statue, the cave is now empty, though careful searching reveals lizard-like bones at the back of the cave.
		* If restored, he will be grateful but confused.  He is Clarus, now 1,522 years old and does not speak Archontean.

Clarus, ancient Set guardsman (see new monsters), as a 2nd-level male Archontean fighter: SZ M; AL LE; AC 4; MV 120’; HD 2; HP 20; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (short sword), 2-7 (javelin). Special defense: fanaticism. Abilities: STR 16, INT 9, WIS 11, DEX 15, CON 16, CHA 8. Possessions: red Set Armor (see Arden Vul items); short sword; javelin; purse with 45 ancient silver pennies (see Arden Vul items). Clarus only speaks Mithric.

### 4-95: Statuary

* This cave is level with the main tunnel and empty other than 6 petrified persons.
	* 2 Set guardsmen, a Set acolyte, a female thief, an owlbear, and a true varumani in armor.
		* All are ancient, the youngest (the owlbear) died over 900 years ago.
	* A strange breeze blows east to west, carrying the smell of burnt cinnamon.

Horatio, Set guardsman (see new monsters), as a 2nd-level Archontean fighter: SZ M; AL LE; AC 3; MV 120’; HD 2; HP 18; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (short sword), 2-7 (javelin). Abilities: STR 16, INT 9, WIS 11, DEX 12, CON 16, CHA 10. Possessions: red Set armor (see Arden Vul items) and wooden shield; short sword; javelin; purse with 15 ancient silver pennies (see Arden Vul items).
* Horatio speaks only Mithric.

Lucinda, ancient Set guardsman (see new monsters), as a 2nd-level female Archontean fighter: SZ M; AL LE; AC 3; MV 120’; HD 2; HP 17; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (short sword), 2-7 (javelin). Abilities: STR 17, INT 11, WIS 8, DEX 14, CON 16, CHA 15. Possessions: red Set Armor (see Arden Vul items) and wooden shield; short sword; javelin; purse with 25 ancient silver pennies (see Arden Vul items).
* Lucinda speaks only Mithric.

Blutus, an ancient Set acolyte (see new monsters), as a 3rd-level Archontean cleric of Set: SZ M; AL LE; AC 4; MV 120’; HD 3; HP 19; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (mace) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Abilities: STR 15, INT 9, WIS 15, DEX 10, CON 10, CHA 9. Possessions: Set armor (see Arden Vul items); footman’s mace; light crossbow; acolyte’s was stick (see new magic items); purse with 5 ancient gold solidi and 15 ancient silver pennies (see Arden Vul items for both); and a silver holy symbol of Set (10 gp). Spells prayed for: command, cure light wounds, curse (reverse of bless), protection from good; hold person, silence 15’ radius.
* Blutus speaks only Mithric.

Pharastina, 7th-level female Thorcin thief: SZ M; AL CN; AC 4; MV 120’; HD 7; HP 39; #AT 1; Dmg 3-8 (short sword +2), or 2-5 (daggers +1). Abilities: STR 13, INT 17, WIS 15, DEX 17, CON 15, CHA 11. Thief skills: PP 65%, OL 62%, F/RT 50%, MS 60%, HS 48%, HN 25%, CW 94%, RL 35%. Possessions: leather armor +1; a set of 6 throwing daggers +1; a curved short sword +2; a potion of gaseous form; and a clan symbol of a crane.
* Pharastina was the sister of the famed warrior and mercenary Phagtro (see World of Archontos appendix), and a minor hero in her own right. She speaks poor Mithric but is fluent in an obscure dialect of Thorcin.

1 owlbear: SZ L; AL N; AC 5; MV 120’; HD 5+2; HP 29; #AT 3; Dmg 1-6/1-6/2-12. Special attacks: hug.

Ludrig, a true varumani (see new monsters) SZ L; AL LN; AC 2; MV 90’; HD 8; HP 60; #AT 3 or 1; Dmg 3-6/3-6/4-10 or 6-24 (two-handed sword, 2-20+4). Special defenses: surprised only on 1 in 6; save as 8th-level fighter or 8th-level magic user, whichever is better; immune to cold, poison, charm, hold, feeblemind, confusion, and other mind-affecting magic; regenerate 3 HP/rd; infravision. Possessions: huge two-handed sword; ring mail; troll thegn’s passport (see Arden Vul items); 3 ancient octagonal platinum coins (see Arden Vul items); a sack of 20 citrine gems worth 50 gp each; and a 12-folio Varumani-Archontean wordlist.
* Ludrig is quite intelligent, and fluent in Mithric. He served as an advisor to the Archonteans during the period in which the troll thegn (7-30) accepted imperial suzerainty. Ludrig’s appearance at the varumani court (7-75) would create a major stir; still, once his identity was established, many varumani would shun him as a collaborator.

### 4-96: Xorn Feeding Zone

* This chamber is 8 degrees colder than the surrounding caves, fertile conditions for a psychotropic pale-blue lichen, blue haze (flora), covering walls, floor, and ceiling.
	* 2 xorn have become addicted to the lichen and wandered the chamber in a drugged stupor, snacking aimlessly on the lichen (20 doses present).
	* The xorn respond to offers of gems or precious metals, but attack those who disturb their stash (i.e., the lichen).

2 xorn: SZ M; AL N; AC -2; MV 90’; HD 7+7; HP 55, 49; #AT 4; Dmg 1-3/1-3/1-3/6-24. Special attacks: surprise on 1-5. Special defenses: immune to fire and cold; half damage from electricity; travel through stone.

### 4-97: Cave of Fungi and Lichen 

* This large cavern is home to numerous species of mushroom and lichen.
	* There are red veil and aqua vitae mushrooms (flora) scattered among the larger species, a few of which are edible.
	* The escaped slaves them for food and fuel.
* Among the stalks dwell 8 fungal foresters; not necessarily hostile.

4 spotted fungal foresters (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 6; MV 30’ on rock, 90’ in fungal forests; HD 4; HP 27, 25, 23, 21; #AT 1; Dmg 2-12.

2 blue fungal foresters (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 6; MV 30’ on rock, 90’ in fungal forests; HD 6; HP 35, 34; #AT 1; Dmg 2-12. Special attacks: spore cloud (stun).

1 yellow fungal forester (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 6; MV 30’ on rock, 90’ in fungal forests; HD 6; HP 35; #AT 1; Dmg 2-12. Special defenses: spore cloud (missile/spell defense).

1 black fungal foresters (see new monsters): SZ L; AL N; AC 4; MV 30’ on rock, 90’ in fungal forests; HD 8; HP 53; #AT 1; Dmg 4-16. Special attacks: spore clouds (stunning, and missile/spell defense).

##### 4-97a: Sunken Pit

* This area is sunken 20’ below the floor of the main mushroom cave.
	* The pit is 10 degrees warmer and home to small yellow mushrooms called mind eaters (flora).
	* A scrawny escaped slave named Michael is sitting in their midst, face dusted yellow, rocking back and forth while singing little bits of nonsense.
		* Michael ate of the mind eaters and lost his mind; he is slowly starving to death.
		* He backs away from PCs but might (50%) attack if his ‘food’ is threatened.

Crazy-Man Michael, an insane Archontean ex-slave: SZ M; AL N; AC 9; MV 120’; HD 1-1; HP 4; #AT 1; Dmg 1-3 (bone knife). 

##### 4-97b: Ledge 

* This ledge is 20’ above the floor of the fungus cave and is covered with two varieties of lichen, one red and one grey.
	* These lichen are symbiotic; when in large enough concentrations (as here), they can issue a telepathic collective thought-impulse to all those within a 10’ radius.
		* The lichen-mind is rather alien, and must be successfully understood before negotiation can occur.
	* The lichen will demand passage (in 10’-diameter sections of each species) to a new location (e.g. the Great Cavern 3-162, 3-172) in return for information.
		* The information is can impart is the location of a ‘being like you, although silent.’  They refer to a limed-over skeleton at the far north of their ledge, difficult to notice without help.
		* It takes several hours of careful scraping and suitable carrying cases, collect the lichen.  It will be quite particular about their new home: it must be cool, not too busy, and not too out-of-the-way.
	* The skeleton is of a hero of the ancient age, Chramn the Hunter, who died of wounds incurred in fighting a basilisk (now dead).
		* Two-handed sword +2, a basilisk horn, and an imperial rescript, carefully folded up in a leather pouch.
			* The rescript reads (Mithric): “What the bearer has done, he has done for the good of the Empire. Signed, L., Logothete of the Drome”.

* GM Note: The rescript is of potentially enormous value, as it could easily be used by unscrupulous parties to justify all manner of actions in the name of the Drome.
	* Should a current logothete of the Drome become aware of this usage, a reckoning will be in order.
	* Leonidas was logothete of the Drome in Archontos in the year 1653 AEP.

Telepathic lichen (see above).

### 4-98: Lair of the Boalisk

* An albino boalisk makes its home in a cave located just to the east of the pond.
	* This dangerous predator is fearless and willing to take on large potential prey.
	* Its familiarity with the area gives it a +1 chance to surprise.

1 albino boalisk (40%): SZ L; AL N; AC 5; MV 120’; HD 5+1; HP 33; #AT 2; Dmg 1-3/2-7. Special attacks: constriction; gaze attack causes mummy rot.

X / 33

### 4-99: Clear Pond

* Clear and deep (35’), this pond is home to numerous blind cavefish.
	* Both the slaves and the boalisk get most of their nutrients here.

Albino boalisk (60%): for stats see 4-98.

### 4-100: Escaped Slaves

* A small group of slaves, escaped from the clutches of the cult of Set, have established a community here in this pair of caves that open 30’ above the clear pond (4-99).
	 	* A fire made of mushroom stalks crackles in the western-most ell of the cave, producing lots of smoke.  Mushroom stalk torches (taken from 4-97) hang near the entrance and in the northern ell.
	* The community has stolen or looted several important items.
		* A large keg of lamp oil (2/3 used); some jury-rigged cookware (made of helmets and the like), a barrel of dried meat, 4 suits of red Set armor (av items), 4 long swords, 2 short swords, a dozen knives, a wand of enemy detection (20 charges), and a wand of fire (10 charges). 
		* Aside from the weapons listed above, they are armed with bone clubs and simple spears.
* There are 25 individuals; mostly human commoners, but with 3 goblins, 1 lizardman, and a beastman (sheep brother).
	* The leaders of the community are three classed individuals.
		* Theophrastus, a peaceful cleric, was taken by a Set patrol out in the valley below the Halls, and is largely ignorant of the Halls save for the Precincts of Set.
		* Jostri and Hexameros are adventurers who worked their way (separately) into the Halls from the cliff face (EX-15).
	* The community is fiercely protective of its members, but anxious to escape the Halls.
		* They have established a fairly safe but still precarious life; fishing in the pond (avoiding the boalisk in 4-98), harvesting fungi and lichen from 4-97, and occasionally hunting lizards or ambushing Set patrols in the surrounding caves.
		* When venturing out, they always travel in groups of five, each group carrying one of four bone whistles crafted by Jostri.  If they run into difficulties, they blow the whistle and bring the classed leaders running (cautiously) to assist. 
		* If the boalisk (4-98) is proven to be defeated, the community will be extremely grateful, treating the heroes as having +4 CHA.
	* The leaders will negotiate happily with good-aligned PCs, exchanging labor, information and possibly one or both wands for food, and aid departing the Halls.
		* They might ask for help ‘saving’ their former comrade, now known sadly, but affectionately, as Crazy-Man Michael (4-97a); sadly he cannot be saved.
		* They know about the exit down the Long Stairs (4-19), but have been unable to figure out a plan to sneak past the Forum of Set.

Theophrastus, 6th-level male Archontean cleric of Demma: SZ M; AL LG; AC 4; MV 60’; HD 6; HP 49; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (footman’s flail). Abilities: STR 15, INT 8, WIS 16, DEX 9, CON 16, CHA 16. Possessions: Set armor (see Arden Vul items); footman’s flail; scroll of knit bones (see new spells). Spells: cure light wounds(x2), light, purify food and drink, resist cold; augury, chant, hold person, silence 15’ radius, slow poison; create food and water (x2).

Jostri the skald, 2nd-level male Wiskin thief: SZ M; AL N; AC 8; MV 120’; HD 2; HP 8; #AT 1; Dmg 1-4 (dagger). Abilities: STR 9, INT 11, WIS 13, DEX 16, CON 10, CHA 15. Thief skills: PP 
35%, OL 34%, F/RT 25%, MS 21%, HS 15%, HN 10%, CW 86%. Possessions: dagger.

Hexameros, 3rd-level male Archontean fighter: SZ M; AL LN; AC 5; MV 90’; HD 3; HP 25; #AT 1; Dmg 2-9. Abilities: STR 16, INT 12, WIS 10, DEX 9, CON 16, CHA 10. Possessions: stolen Set armor (see Arden Vul items); long sword.

1 lizardman: SZ M; AL N; AC 5; MV 60’, 120’ swimming; HD 2+1; HP 12; #AT 1 or 3; Dmg by weapon, or 1-2/1-2/1-8.

1 beastman trooper (see new monsters): SZ S; AL LN; AC 6; MV 90’; HD 1+1; HP: 8, 7, 7, 6, 6, 5; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6 (club). Special attacks: tactics.

3 goblins: SZ S; AL LE; AC 6; MV 60’; HD 1-1; HP 5, 4, 3; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6.

17 Thorcin humans, of which 10 are men and 7 are women: SZ M; AL varies; AC 10; MV 120’; HD 1-1; HP 7, 7, 6(x3), 5(x3), 4(x3), 3(x3), 2(x3); #AT 1; Dmg 1-6 (club). Possessions: clubs.

3 Thorcin children, noncombatants: AC 10, HP 1.

## 4-101 to 4-104: Ambassadors’ Residences

* A set of chambers just off the Forum, reserved for the lodging of important ambassadors.
	* The hallway, common area, and individual rooms all feature 20’ ceilings.
	* The common area outside the chambers is furnished with two low coffee tables, a small cabinet, wall hangings with a few bits of promotional imagery, and eight comfortable chairs, two sized for large creatures.
		* Hangings: an ornate scroll paen to the greatness of Set; a series of illustrations of great moments in the cult of Set, the plucking of a sad-looking ibis, etc.
	* Two of the chambers have spy holes for the priests of Set to spy on their guests.
	* The Set cult typically uses the ‘gift’ of residence in these chambers as a way of wooing important or powerful guests.
		* Those from weaker cultures or institutions are flatly rebuffed, as are those subject to the cult’s casual racism (no goblins or lizardmen here).
		* Powerful, high-level, PCs who have done favors for (or promised favors to) the cult might - might! - be permitted to stay here.

### 4-101: Emissaries from the Troll Thegn

* Four varumani (three lesser, one true) reside here as quasi-permanent ambassadors from the court of the troll thegn (see 7-75).
	* The walls are a neutral ochre color so as not to offend.
	* Four beds; a table with dice, cards, and several bottles of good ale; waste pails; a locked chest; and the services of a goblin slave.
		* Chest (locked): 10 1-lb platinum bars (250 gp each), a sack of 143 ancient gold solidi, 10 passes to the troll thegn’s court (av items), a periapt of proof against poison, a wand of detect lie (56 charges), and a rudishva communication array (tech) they use to report back to the thegn.
	* A set of spy holes is concealed in the stonework of the east wall (see 4-101a). 
* The lesser varumani defer to the true varumani, Yoburra, the one entrusted with actual diplomacy, being far smarter than his lesser cousins.
	* The lesser varumani have devised a dartboard out of their previous servant, a human named Max.
	* All four see this posting as a joke; none of them respect the Set priests.
		* They enjoy lolling around, pretending to care about the machinations of the Set cult.  They do pay close attention to first-time visitors to the forum, ready to keep the thegn apprised of potential threats and/or potential allies.

3 lesser varumani (see new monsters): SZ L; AL LE; AC 4; MV 90’; HD 8; HP 58, 57, 52; #AT 3 or 1; Dmg 3-6/3-6/4-10 or 7-22 (mattock, 3-18+4). Special defenses: 33% resistant to mind-
affecting magic; immune to cold and poison; save as 8th-level fighters or 8th-level magic users, whichever is better; regenerate 3 HP/rd; infravision. Possessions: mattocks.

Yoburra, a true varumani (see new monsters): SZ L; AL LN; AC 2; MV 90’; HD 8; HP 60; #AT 3 or 1; Dmg 3-6/3-6/4-10 or 6-24 (two-handed sword, 2-20+4). Special defenses: surprised only on 1 in 6; save as 8th-level fighter or 8th-level magic user, whichever is better; immune to cold, poison, charm, hold, feeblemind, confusion, and other mind-affecting magic; regenerate 3 HP/rd; infravision. Possessions: huge two-handed sword, ring mail., chest key

1 goblin slave named Quarm: SZ S; AL LE; AC 6; MV 60’; HD 1-1; HP 3; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6.

##### 4-101a: Spy Passages

* These narrow, rough passages allow the Set cult to spy on emissaries in 4-101 and 4-102.
	* The stairs descending to area 4-19 are unusually steep.
	* A wooden shelf set in the wall between the two sets of spy holes holds a stylus, inkpot, and unbound parchment quire.
		* The folios of the quire are divided into two columns, one entitled ‘trolls’ and the other ‘giants’.
			* The observations are mostly mundane, with a few of interest.
			* Folio 7: the varumani emissaries talked about the plans of Varboka, the troll thegn (7-30), to enslave the goblins.
				* Worth 4,500 gp to King Weskenim (SL4-22).
			* Folio 6: the giant emissaries have decided to accept the offer of alliance tendered by the high priestess (4-51) and to initiate attacks against the Archontean outposts beginning in the next harvest season.
				* Worth 5,000 gp to Keko the Lame in Narsileon.
	* Showing the spy notes to the giants brings mere shrugs; they expect that sort of thing.  Showing them to the varumani causes Varboka to withdraw his emissaries and to prepare for conflict with the Set cult.
		* GM Note: Stephania’s proposed alliance with the giants could be used to develop further adventures outside of Arden Vul.
	* Secret Door (east): easy to locate from this side (1 in 4), pulled inward to open.
* 25% chance a low-ranking member of the Guild of Service is here, spying.

1 guildsman, as a 2nd-level male Archontean fighter: SZ M; AL LE; AC 8; MV 120’; HD 2; HP 16; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (spears, clubs). Possessions: leather armor; spear; and club. Special: he 
has +1 to damage from STR.

### 4-102: Giant Emissaries

* Two frost giant ambassadors are resident here.
	* Two beds, a chest, a table and two chairs, a huge polar bear fleece, two bundles of animal skins/rugs, and waste pails.
		* The beds are too small, and the giants have pushed them together to make a lounging area, on which sleeps their pet winter wolf.
		* Chest: wand of frost (32 charges), 50 pieces of amber (50 gp each), a mixed pile of coins (300 gp), a keg of fiery brandy, giant-sized equipment; winter wolf pelt (500 gp).
	* They have had their winter wolf spray frost throughout it to make it more homey.
	* A set of spy holes is concealed in the stonework of the east wall (see 4-101A).
* Hjall and Hedin are secretive and largely stay in their chamber.
	* The giants do not like the varumani, nor do they particularly care for the Set priests.
	* Officially sent by their jarl to negotiate an alliance with Set against the Archontean empire (see 4-101a).
		* They have a secondary motive: the jarl’s wife, with the gift of sight, has predicted a dangerous potential ally or enemy will appear in the Forum in the next three months.  This ally or enemy will be a female human (or half-elven) magic user with raven-black hair.
			* They aren’t sure what the premonition is about, but have orders to seize the object of the premonition and return with her to the jarl.
			* Any human mage who fits these features may be in danger.
	* They don’t like having to stay underground and are anxious to find the subject of the premonition and beat a retreat.

Hjall and Hedin, frost giants: SZ L; AL CE; AC 4; MV 120’; HD 10+1-4; HP 72, 68; #AT 1; Dmg 4-24. Special attacks: hurl rocks (2-20 dmg). Special defenses: immune to cold.

Snowy, a winter wolf: SZ L; AL N(E); AC 5; MV 180’; HD 6; HP 40; #AT 1; Dmg 2-8. Special attacks: frost blast. Special defenses: immune to cold.

### 4-103: Uninhabited Chamber

* This chamber for ambassadors is empty.
* It has two beds, a table and chairs, a chest, and other necessities.

### 4-104: Uninhabited Chamber

* This chamber for ambassadors is empty.
* It has two beds, a table and chairs, a chest, and other necessities.

## Level 4: 105 - 106

### 4-105: Stair of Commerce with Niches 

* This broad, 20’-wide stairs rises from the chasm of Set (4-119) to the Forum itself (4-2).
	* It provides the primary access to the Forum from both outside and within Arden Vul.
	* The marble stairs, worn down the center by the tread of countless feet over the centuries, are brightly lit with continual light.
	* 6 semi-circular niches line the stair; each holds an impressive 5'-tall stone bust of a former Set priest atop a 5'-tall stone table.
		* They depict youthful humans in an otherworldly, idealized way (wide eyes, vacant gazes, smooth faces, etc.), the modern style of imperial portraiture, as opposed to super-realistic style of the old empire.
			* Two are female, one wears a skullcap, a few boast scarves, and one is depicted in a cylindrical headdress.
		* They are the six most important high priests of Set since the cult’s modern resurgence some 90 years ago.
	* Secret Door (west): in the niche occupied by the bust of Cilicius Gresto, a high priest of Set from some fifty years in the past.
		* Pressing a button in the fold of Cilicius’s scarf opens the 4' square door.  It leads to a short passage and another secret door (see 4-110).
* 20% chance of encountering another group on the stairs.
	* 33% a squad of Set guardsmen with a sergeant, 66% a group of visitors (roll on Table 1 at area 4-2).
	* The guardsmen will take little interest in the party unless it acts with hostility.
	* Visitors’ reactions should be determined normally.

Possible Inhabitants:
* 1 Set sergeant (see new monsters), as a 5th-level Archontean fighter: SZ M; AL LE; AC 3; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 3-8 (mace +1), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: Set armor (see Arden Vul items) and wooden shield; footman’s mace +1; spear; light crossbow with 20 bolts.
* 4 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts.
* Visitors to Forum (see area 4-2, table 1)

### 4-106: Spiked and Locked Door

* A new wooden door, locked and spiked from the side of the Stair of Commerce (4-105).
	* The carved into the lintel in formal, majuscule letters (Mithric): “Set Vanquishes the Serpent”.  On the door, is hastily painted (Archontean): “No access. Stay out! This means you!”
		* The Set cult has barred this door to the third mystery due to its inability to defeat the behir (4-111).
	* Keys to the door are held by the leaders of the cult of Set (4-51, 4-47, 4-56, 4-57).

## Level 4: 107 to 111

* These rooms are dark, silent, and filled with inches of dust.
	* Several sets of footprints run from 4-106 to 4-111, still filled with decades of dust.
	* The only recemt tracks are those of the behir (4-111), a giant constrictor snake (4-109), and dozens of small normal-sized lizards.

### 4-107: Open Door and Warning

* The door to this chamber is open about a foot.  Subtle serpent tracks enter it.
* This former residential suite has clearly not been used in centuries. 
	* Broken furniture lies everywhere, covered in piles of dust.
	* Inspection shows some of it is scorched.
	* An enormous serpent skin (of a 15’ snake) lies in the dust.

### 4-108: Shattered and Charred Door

* This wooden door hangs crazily on its hinges.
	* It is very old and shows signs of being blasted apart and scorched by electricity.

### 4-109: Serpent’s Lair

* The door to this chamber is locked and stuck (blocked from inside by a pile of debris).
* Once the high priest’s sumptuously decorated chamber, it is now lair to an enormous giant python, the descendant of one of the sacrificial serpents now living in symbiosis with the behir.
	* The serpent’s nest is littered with bones, mostly small and reptilian, but several large and mammalian.
		* -1 attack from the jumble of brittle bones and desiccated furniture.
		* Among the bones: 26 gp, 37 sp, a garnet (50 gp), an emerald (300 gp), a snapped wand of magic missiles, a dagger of venom, and a guard cap (new).
	* An ancient fresco on the north wall is faded and worn: it depicts the third mystery in a set of images.
		* Western end: a high priest in red robes and red conical hat strides forth with a was stick.
		* Center: a huge serpent emerges from a hole in a wall, while the red-garbed priest raises a large knife.
		* Eastern end: the priest stands atop of the snake's corpse, holding the knife and the snake’s decapitated head over his head.
		* Above the images is written (Mithric): “Set vanquishes the serpent.”
	* The western wall has crumbled, and a 5’-diameter hole allows access to natural tunnels beyond.

1 giant constrictor snake (50% chance): SZ L; AL N; AC 5; MV 90’; HD 6+1; HP 39; #AT 2; Dmg 1-4/2-8. Special attacks: constriction.

X / 39

### 4-110: Preparation Chamber

* Here the high priest conducted the preparatory rituals (including propitious sacrifices and ablutions) prior to conducting the third mystery. 
	* Western side: a dry, sunken pool (3’ deep, 8’ square) occupies the center.
		* The preferred place for the giant constrictor snake to eliminate larger prey.
		* The pool is filled with various bones.
			* Mixed in: a pair of insalubrious-looking boots of insulation (new).
	* Eastern side: broken furniture, a painted screen, and a variety of ratty robes and ceremonial clothes.
	* Center: opposite the entrance passage is a marble altar (4’ tall, 3’ wide, and 6’ long).
		* It bears ancient dried bloodstains.
	* South wall: a mural of the third mystery, with a red-robed high priest stabbing a serpent with an exaggeratedly large dagger.
* The mural and some furniture are damaged (scorched and blasted).

(25%) giant constrictor snake: for stats see 4-109.

### 4-111: 3rd Mystery of Set: The Ritual of the Slaying of the Serpent

* The third of the great mysteries of the cult of Set took place of old in this large cavern.
	* Now it is the territory of a behir, which the priests of Set are unable to dislodge.
	* To the chagrin of Stephania, the third mystery has not been performed since antiquity.
* The chamber of the mystery includes two areas, a worked area and a natural cavern area.
	* The worked area opens from the corridor into a 20’ x 30’ area paved with white and black marble.
		* The western edge of this pavement is 10’ above the floor of the cavern, set off by a low balustrade (3’) of marble.
		* The pavement is covered by centuries of dust, disturbed only by slither marks.
		* Marble stairs lead down to a semi-circle of mosaic covered with dirt and dust.
			* Numerous tracks cross it - rodent, serpent, and lizard (behir) tracks.
			* If swept clean, the mosaic shows Set wielding a ritual dagger and holding the corpse of a huge serpent.
	* The natural area extends in an arc around the mosaic, culminating in a rocky western wall perforated by numerous holes.
		* Most of the holes seem fit for rats or snakes.  There is one larger one on the southwestern face.
		* Three low knobs rise from rocky floor (3-5’ high). 
		* The rough ceiling rises 35’ from the cavern floor.
		* Searching the natural area reveals 6 skeletons, picked clean by rats.
			* One is the high priest before Stephania (Keladorus of Arcturos), a brave fool who attempted to enter the chamber and best the behir.
				* Ring of Set named Fragas (new), a scroll (curse item, new), a copper, jade, and lapis necklace (200 gp).
				* Nearby under inches of dust: the sacred ritual dagger of the Third Mystery rests (1,000 gp to the cult of set; 50 gp to others).
			* 3 are the high priest’s guards (x3), still in Set armor (av items) blasted by powerful energy.
			* 2 skeletons are ancient; a pair of adventurers.
				* Long sword +1, 3 arrows of striking (new) stuffed in a wooden scroll case; blasted and useless chain mail, a pouch with 3 potions (invisibility, clairvoyance, clairaudience), a rotting sack with 179 gp.

The Third Mystery
* In antiquity a high priest would re-enact the dramatic mythological moment in which Set slew the great serpent, Apep, and in so doing became the protector of humanity.
* In emulation of this event, and with an audience of cultists and visitors watching from the pavement, the high priest would descend to the mosaic and slay a semi-wild snake driven from one of the cliff holes by a specially-trained snake-handler.
	* Marking oneself in its blood would confer Set's blessing and power.
* When the Set cult returned to Arden Vul in the past century, it found that a behir had invaded the area; efforts to drive off the behir have failed.
	* This beast was sent by Apep to scorn Set's "mastery" of serpents.

24 giant rats: SZ S; AL N(E); AC 7; MV 120’; HD 1-4 HP; HP 4(x6), 3(x6), 2(x6), 1(x6); #At 1; Dmg 1-3. Special attacks: 5% chance of disease.

(25%) Giant constrictor snake: for stats see 4-109.

(20%, noise draws it swiftly from 4-112c) 1 behir: SZ L; AL NE; AC 4; MV 150’; HD 12; HP 85; #AT 2 or 7; damage 2-8/2-5 or 2-8/1-6(x6). Special attacks: lightning bolt. Special defenses: immune to electricity and poison.

## Level 4: 112 - 120

### 4-112: Lair of the Behir

* The behir makes its lair in this set of caverns and tunnels.
	* The area is notably cooler and moister than other areas of Level 4. 
	* The large caves are maze of rocky projections, dangerous fissures, and small pools of water.  The rough, uneven floor is extremely difficult for humanoids to navigate.
	* The terrain has made it all the harder for the Set cult to dislodge the behir.
* The behir will initially in 4-111, 4-112c, 4-113, 4-114, or 4-115 (equal chance for each).
	* Unless exceptionally stealthy, the behir will hear people clambering into the tunnel to 4-112a and will arrive in 1-4 rounds to aggressively defend its territory.
	* It would take great skill and luck to surprise the behir in 4-112c.
	* If the behir is bloodied (50% HP), it retreats into the mist in 4-115.

##### 4-112a: Larder

* This open cavern stinks terribly of decaying meat.
* It rises 10’ feet from the tunnel to 4-111 before dropping off to the west and south.  This elevation change and the slick rock formations make it hard to navigate.
	* Sound in the chamber attracts the behir in 1-4 rounds.
* Numerous skeletal and fleshly remains are scattered in nooks and crannies.
	* Most are rats and other small dungeon vermin, but a few are human-sized.
	* Every turn of searching, discover (d4): 1) 1-100 coins; 2) a potion (33% chance dried up); 3) a gem (10 gp); 4) an item of cultural or historical interest.
* Tracking can discern the behir's regular passage through the northern portion of the cave (to reach the rats at 4-111).

##### 4-112b: Dripping Cave

* This wide, rocky cavern has a 5’-wide tunnel leading to a hole in the cliff face (4-111).
	* There are signs of the behir’s passing.

##### 4-112c: Lair

* The behir makes its main lair in this cave.
	* There is a pool of fresh water in the southwest extension.
	* The tunnel from 4-112a rises 15’ and culminates in a narrow, 4'-tall squeeze into the main chamber at 4-112c.

1 behir: SZ L; AL NE; AC 4; MV 150’; HD 12; HP 85; #AT 2 or 7; damage 2-8/2-5 or 2-8/1-6(x6). Special attacks: lightning bolt. Special defenses: immune to electricity and poison.
* In Gullet: 16 aquamarines (100 gp each), 3 tiger eyes (10 gp each), 5 moonstones (50 gp each); a large gold comb studded with citrines (7,000 gp); a silver-and-gold toe ring (1,100 gp), and a periapt of proof against poison.

### 4-113: Bright Cave

* The long tunnel from 4-112a snakes downward 60’ to this cavern.
	* It is lit by a fluorescent glow from a strange variety of mold growing on the rocks.
		* The fluorescence is calming and peaceful.  Those entering must save vs spells or fall into a stupor lasting 4-8 turns.
		* The behir or giant python might arrive while one or more PCs are dazed.

### 4-114: Pool

* This cavern is filled with a 30’-deep pool of clear water. 
	* Western exit: near the ceiling of the cavern, 20’ above the water level.  Unwary folk might walk off the ledge and into the water. 
	* Northern exit: leads to a long, snaky tunnel that rises over many rocky projections before reaching 4-116. 
	* Southern exit: a small tunnel 15’ above the water level that leads to a hole in the wall of the chasm of Set (4-121).
		* The chasm access is 20’ below that of the platforms (4-119 and 4-120).

### 4-115: Mist-Filled Cave

* The stone of this cavern is composed of unusual concentrations of iron, strontium, and arcanum (new) which has lent it some strange features.
	* A heavy mist occupies both lobes of the cave, appearing almost solid, as if molecules of ore were precipitating in and out of a gaseous state.
		* Light shining on the mist will show a shimmering veil of glinting, crackling, quasi-opaque ‘vapor’.
		* The mist is restorative to the behir (healing it 1d6 / round) and absorbing a charge from it.
			* This shocks others in the mist each round (save for half): 2d8 if the behir is present, or 1d4 from residual charge if it is absent.
		* Beings (other than the behir) must save vs doom or be teleported with a flash of electricity (roll each person's destination separately).
			* 1) island in the lake, Level 3 (3-164a)
			* 2) random cave in Sub-Level 3
			* 3) the pyramid of Thoth, surface ruins (AV-15)
			* 4) the floor of the Great Chasm (9-1)
			* 5) the Hall of Forty Columns (5-6)
			* 6) GM’s choice
		* Those carrying at least 1 lb of arcanum are immune to both shock and translocation by the mists.
	* At the far end of the southeastern lobe is an 8”-tall solid gold statuette of a camel (new), dropped by a previous visitor.

(20%) 1 behir: for stats see 4-112c.

### 4-116: Lichen Cave

* This wide spot in the tunnels is damp and slick.
	* A yellow lichen grows all over the walls and ceiling. It glows softly, imparting a bit of light to the chamber and is harmless and surprisingly nutritious.

### 4-117: Tunnel Down to 5-117

* The tunnel forks here, with one branch ending in a slight spur and the other sloping downward sharply to form a steep tunnel that leads to 5-117.
	* The spur ends in a ledge, near the ceiling (hard to detect), on which is a skeleton of an ancient hero of Set, still wearing its rusted red chain mail.
		* It bears a mace of enforced harmony (new), a pouch (31 ancient silver pennies, 11 ancient gold solidi).

### 4-118: Forgotten Hall

* A long-forgotten priest planned this austere hall as the initial stage of his never-completed tomb complex.
	* A dais rises 5’ in three steps at the north end.
	* The walls are undecorated.  A cave-in has revealed a 5’-diameter tunnel to the north.
		* The passage links to the chasm (4-121) 30’ above that of the landings (4-119 and 4-120).
	* The floor is littered with small, gray, knob-like objects.
		* They are digested remnants of chasm cephalopods consumed by the hungry lurker above that dwells here.
	* The lurker above waits for all to enter, but it is so hungry it may leap too early (50%).
		* It surprises on a 1-5.
		* In the creature’s gullet is a badly corroded gold and silver coronet (50 gp).

1 lurker above: SZ L; AL N; AC 6; MV 10’, 90’ flying (Class D); HD 10; HP 68; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: surprise 4 in 6; constriction; suffocation. Special defenses: 90% undetectable 
against stone.

X / 68

2 / 2

### 4-119: North Landing

* This landing is floored in bright mosaics depicting each of the three mysteries of Set and other elements of his iconography.
	* A shimmering, transparent field runs across the width of the landing, 10’ from the edge of the chasm.
		* It is impenetrable from the south, but fully permeable from the north.
		* The command word 'shield' causes the field to fade for 5 rounds.  This is well known to the cult of Set.
	* At the north foot of the bridge is a square of marble incised with lapis lazuli letters (Mithric) on which a random riddle appears:
		* First Riddle: I shelter brave men. With my bloody back I ward off blows, thwarting spears, giving life to some. I lay my body against my lord’s left hand.
		* Second Riddle: I’m by nature solitary, scarred by spear and wounded by sword, weary of battle. Battered by the face of war, my strength holds back hateful enemies. 
	* Delaying in front of the field may (25%) draw a pod of chasm cephalopods.

6 small chasm cephalopods (see new monsters) (25% chance): SZ S; AL N; AC 5; MV 60’ flying (Class A); HD 2; HP 14, 13, 13, 12, 11, 8; #AT 5 (4 tentacles and a beak); Dmg 1-3/1-3/1-3/1-3/1-4; MR 25%. Special attacks: surprise on 1-4.

### 4-120: South Landing

* This landing overlooks the chasm of Set.
	* 25% chance (+5% per turn spent here) chasm cephalopods (new) attack those who dawdle on the landing.

4 small chasm cephalopods (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 5; MV 60’ flying (Class A); HD 2; HP 13, 12, 11, 8; #AT 5 (4 tentacles and a beak); Dmg 1-3/1-3/1-3/1-3/1-4; MR 25%. Special attacks: surprise on 1-4.

2 medium chasm cephalopods (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 5; MV 60’ flying (Class A); HD 4; HP 25, 24; #AT 5 (4 tentacles and a beak); Dmg 1-4/1-4/1-4/1-4/1-6; MR 25%. Special attacks: surprise on 1-4.

##### 4-120a: Red Bridge of Set

* This 8’-wide stone bridge is one of the iconic locations in Arden Vul.
	* Constructed of red granite, it is slender, rising effortlessly above the chasm, anchored on either landing by 8’-tall marble pillars.
	* Balustrades (4’ tall) carved in the shape of standing Set animals flank the bridge.
	* Unless magically dampened, footfalls echo loudly across the chasm.
		* 50% likely to alert the guards at 4-123 and 4-124 of the approach of visitors.

## Level 4: 121 - 135

### 4-121: Chasm of Set

* The chasm drops 100’ below the level of the bridge (4-12), and rises about 50’ above it.
	* The walls are rocky and uneven, and numerous forms of lichen and moss grow here. 
	* The chasm is moist and humid; the sound of dripping echoes loudly throughout.
		* The floor of the chasm is covered by 15’ feet of water. 
			* Numerous small treasures have fallen here over the years (see below).
			* Below the water, a stone archway is cut into the side of the wall and covered by a shimmering veil of energy.
				* The veil is permeable.  Those who enter are instantly transported either to 1) the Roiling Lake (9-65), or 2) the Drowned Cavern (SL6-24) or 3) the elemental plane of water.
				* A pack of lacedons defends the hidden gate.
					* The cult of Set knows of the ghouls, but not the gate.
	* The chasm is home to a small community of chasm cephalopods (those slain elsewhere (e.g., 4-119, 4-120) should be subtracted from this total).
* Note: If the submerged door at AV-39 has been opened, and the southern portion of the swamp drained, the chasm at 4-121 will contain much more water, its level only 30’ below the bridge (4-120a) and landings (4-119 and 4-120).

The treasures in the chasm are hard to locate, and explorating attracts the ghouls.  Some discoveries include:
* A 1’-diameter sphere of platinum inset with jet, garnet, and ivory realistically depicting the continents and islands of Magae (5,000 gp)
* Scattered coins: 119 ancient silver pennies and 71 ancient gold solidi, 53 sp, 27 gp, and 9 pp.
* A crude statuette of a penguin carved from volcanic rock, with two huge jet gems for eyes (250 gp each for the gems, 650 gp for the statuette)
* A metal shield +2
* An icon of kauket (new)
* Acursed blacklight torch (new)
* A scrying ball hidden inside a clay jar (new)
* A wand of alignment detection (43 charges) (new)
* An obsidian skull of comprehension (new).
* (east end of the chasm) a 2’-long, 1”-diameter iron bar (the 3rd lever from 4-127).

10 small chasm cephalopods (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 5; MV 60’ flying (Class A); HD 2; HP 15, 14, 13, 13, 12, 12, 11, 11, 10, 8; #AT 5 (4 tentacles and a beak); Dmg 1-3/1-3/1-3/1-3/1-4; MR 25%. Special attacks: surprise on 1-4.

6 medium chasm cephalopods (see new monsters): SZ M; AL N; AC 5; MV 60’ flying (Class A); HD 4; HP 27, 26, 25, 24, 24, 22; #AT 5 (4 tentacles and a beak); Dmg 1-4/1-4/1-4/1-4/1-6; MR 25%. Special attacks: surprise on 1-4.

12 lacedons: SZ M; AL CE; AC 6; MV 90’, 90’ swimming; HD 2; HP 15, 14, 14, 13(x3), 12(x3), 10, 9, 9; #AT 3; Dmg 1-3/1-3/1-6. Special attacks: paralysis. Special defenses: immune to sleep and charm.

### 4-122: Thothian Teleportation Ring

* A Thothian teleporation ring is set in the floor here (address: BK-RE-BL-WH-YE-GR).
	* No glass activation squares are present.
	* The Set cult is ignorant of it's function, though they know it is powerful magic.

##### 4-122a: Secret Doors and Hidden Staircase to AV-39

* Just south of the landing area are a pair of secret doors.
	* Secret Door (east): opens by inserting a rod into a 1" ceiling hole.  Leads to 4-148.
	* Secret Door (west, locked, -5% to pick): hard to spot (1 in 8).  Key was lost ages ago.
		* It leads to a dusty chamber with a stone spiral staircase that rises 650’ to a ruined cellar in the surface ruins (AV-39).

### 4-123: Guard Chamber

* A detachment of 4 Set guardsmen and an acolyte is on duty here at all times.
	* The chamber is decorated in bright yellow and blue primary colors.
	* The insignia of each military sept of the cult is painted on a wall: the black boar, a head with white face and red hair, and a tornado.
	* A circular table, some benches, two water barrels, several sets of dice (one loaded), a dartboard, and a good supply of jerky.
* They keep the door half-open so as to hear any visitors to the halls of Set.
	* Visitors who are not aggressive will be asked their business.
		* If the acolyte is content that nothing is awry, they read out the Laws of the Forum and a few other random warnings (“Don’t go poking your noses into the private areas”, “Show respect to the Black Boar”, “Watch out for the Breath of Set”, etc.).
		* 20% chance they try to shake down visitors for a toll of 1-10 gp per character.
	* If combat ensues, the denizens of the other guardroom (4-124) immediately emerge to aid their colleagues, and one guard sprints north to warn the rest of the cult.
	* If noise is heard at the north landing (4-119), 25% chance they come to investigate.
		* Could be due to the echo-effect of the bridge (4-120a), combat with chasm cephalopods, etc.
		* If they come, they will be suspicious.  Since the shield curtain (4-119) is porous from the north, they won’t be averse to hurling a few javelins through it.

4 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts. One has the bonds of Set. Another has 3 bolts of fire (see new magic items).

1 Set acolyte (see new monsters), as a 3rd-level Archontean cleric of Set: SZ M; AL LE; AC 4; MV 60’; HD 3; HP 19; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (mace) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Possessions: Set 
armor (see Arden Vul items); footman’s mace; light crossbow; acolyte’s was stick (see new magic items); and a silver holy symbol of Set (10 gp). Spells prayed for: command, cure light 
wounds, curse (reverse of bless), protection from good; hold person, silence 15’ radius.

### 4-124: Guard Chamber

* Identical to 4-123, except that the chamber is decorated with large images of the three mysteries of Set instead.

4 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts. One has the bonds of Set. Another has 3 bolts of fire (see new magic items).

1 Set acolyte (see new monsters), as a 3rd-level Archontean cleric of Set: SZ M; AL LE; AC 4; MV 60’; HD 3; HP 19; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (mace) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Possessions: Set armor (see Arden Vul items); footman’s mace; light crossbow; acolyte’s was stick (see new magic items); and a silver holy symbol of Set (10 gp). Spells prayed for: command, cure light 
wounds, curse (reverse of bless), protection from good; hold person, silence 15’ radius.

### 4-125: Cultists’ Rest

* This is one of the five dormitories for cultists coming to visit the temple of Set and participate in its mysteries (the others are at 4-126, 4-131, 4-132, and 4-133).
	* Each chamber is painted brightly in primary colors, and contains 12 double bunk-beds plus 1-4 chests, 2 large water barrels, and a cloak-rack.

To determine the contents and inhabitants of each dormitory:
* Each dormitory has a 33% chance of being inhabited by 2d12+3 people.
	* At least one dormitory will be inhabited regardless of the dice rolls, however.
	* Each dormitory contains rough bunk-beds sufficient for 24 persons.
		* Ordinarily no more than 40 cultists are present in all dormitories, but higher numbers may indicate a major gathering of the cult with appropriate implications for politics and/or adventuring.
* Origin of the Cultists (d12)
	* 1-6 Group from outside Arden Vul. Roll d10:
		* 1-2: important Archonteans, incognito
		* 3-5: curious local Thorcinga
		* 6: Khumus pilgrims from the far west
		* 7-10: ordinary Archontean humans
	* 7-8 Goblins from Sub-Level 4
	* 9 Lizardman converts from Sub-Level 5
	* 10 NPC adventuring party (select from NPC appendix)
	* 11 1d3 lesser varumani converts from Level 7
	* 12 Other, or GM's choice
* Business of Cultists
	* 1-4 Ordinary cultic sight-seeing
	* 5-6 Conveying an important message from outside Arden Vul
	* 7-8 Bringing an important relic/object
	* 9-11 Personal redemption, or penance
	* 12 Hidden Purpose. Roll d12:
		* 1-2: vendetta or vengeance
		* 3-4: spying …. for whom?
		* 5-6: bringing secret information to cult leaders
		* 7-8: excuse to meet other groups in Forum
		* 9-10: acquire some object
		* 11-12: other or GM’s choice
* Furnishings of the Chamber
	* If a chamber is currently inhabited, cultists will also have their personal treasure.
	* 20% chance a group will be in possession of a significant object or treasure.

Up to 40 Set cultists (see new monsters): SZ M; AL LE; AC 9; MV 90’; HD 1; HP 7(x5), 6(x8), 5(x10), 4(x10), 3(x7); #AT 1; Dmg 1-4 (dagger) or 2-7 (flail) or 1-6 (staff). Special attacks: 
fanaticism. Possessions: padded armor; daggers; flails or staves.

### 4-126: Cultists’ Rest

* See description at 4-125.

### 4-127: Chasm View

* This ancient chamber overlooks the chasm of Set, currently used as a lounge for cultists.
	* The ceiling is covered with mother-of-pearl, making its three torches reflect wildly through the room.
	* The walls are freshly painted in light-blue wash, with gold stars and mystical symbols.
	* The floor is covered by a mosaic of a Set priest floating in the air between two cliffs.
	* 8 stools and 3 circular wooden tables; all battered and worn.
	* On the southeast wall are two iron levers and a hole for a third is next to them.
		* The levers have two positions (up and down; currently both down).
		* The third lever currently rest at the bottom of the chasm, see 4-121.  Any metal rod 1” in diameter and about 2’ long can be substituted. 
	* The southeastern corner of the chamber is open to the chasm (4-121)
		* A 3’-tall balustrade runs along the chasm edge.
			* Strangely, a 5’-wide section of the balustrade is missing.
			* The balustrade is 20’ above the landings at 4-119 and 4-120.
			* 20’ from the balustrade, a stone chest apparents to float in the air (actually resting on an invisible platform of stone), .
				* One might infer the balustrade opening is meant to lead (somehow) to the floating chest.
	* An invisible stone bridge connects the balustrade both to the chest platform and to the opposite side of the chasm.
		* It is 2’ below the lip of the balustrade; simply tapping where one imagines a bridge might be will not detect it.
		* Going out on the bridge automatically attracts the chasm cephalopods.
		* The invisible bridge is sturdy, if disconcerting, and leads at a slight angle across the chasm to the concealed door of the passage leading to 4-147a.
		* The chest rests on a slight widening of the bridge 12’ south of the balustrade.
			* The chest is locked and trapped with a gust of wind rune.
			* eight 2-lb platinum bars worth 500 gp each, a helm of underwater action, a pure white tear of Kauket (new) mounted in silver and wrapped in a piece of chamois-cloth.

The Levers (requires all 3 to produce any effect)
* down-down-down: ‘neutral’; no effects. 
* up-down-down: a magic mouth intones (Mithric), “Walk”
	* For 1-3 turns a high, keening sound emits from a the magic mouth; it deters chasm cephalopods, rendering the path to the chest safe.
* down-up-down: a magic mouth intones (Mithric), “The wind of Set eliminates those who do not belong!"
	* A gust of wind spell based at the foot of the stairs from 4-129, is directed towards the chasm.
* down-down-up: a magic mouth intones (Mithric), “The cleansing fire of Set removes the unbelievers!"
	* a moving wall of fire appears by the stairs leading from 4-129 and moves 5’ per round towards the balustrade.
* other four positions: a magic mouth intones (Mithric), “Unbelievers shall be slain!”
	* a cloudkill spell activates in the center of the chamber.

3-12 Set cultists (33%): SZ M; AL LE; AC 9; MV 90’; HD 1; HP 7, 7, 6(x4), 5(x3), 4, 4, 3; #AT 1; Dmg 1-4 (dagger) or 2-7 (flail) or 1-6 (staff). Special attacks: fanaticism. Possessions: padded 
armor; daggers; flails or staves.

6 small chasm cephalopods (see new monsters), potentially drawn by manipulation of the levers: SZ S; AL N; AC 5; MV 60’ flying (Class A); HD 2; HP 14, 13, 13, 12, 11, 8; #AT 5 (4 tentacles and a beak); Dmg 1-3/1-3/1-3/1-3/1-4; MR 25%. Special attacks: surprise on 1-4.

### 4-128: Lesser Shrine

* High Priestess Stephania has set up a shrine here for the use of the cultists.
	* By the east wall are two 8’-tall painted statues of wood, cloth and papier-mâché.
		* One is of Set in his Set animal guise; the other is a white-faced, red-haired man.
		* Between the statues is a stone altar, stained with blood, on which is a copper bowl and a copper knife.
	* The walls are painted with human devotees bringing offerings to the statues.
	* The entire place radiates evil.
	* Near the south wall is a 5’-diameter hole in the floor covered with boards held down by chunks of rock.
		* The hole leads down 10’ before reaching the ceiling of the burial crypt (4-139a), with a drop of 20' to reach the floor.
* The cultists generally disdain this shrine, preferring to visit the ‘real thing’ further north.

2 Set acolytes (see new monsters), as 3rd-level Archontean clerics of Set: SZ M; AL LE; AC 4; MV 60’; HD 3; HP 19, 18; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (mace) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Possessions: Set 
armor (see Arden Vul items); footman’s mace; light crossbow; acolyte’s was stick (see new magic items); and a silver holy symbol of Set (10 gp). Spells prayed for: command, cure light 
wounds, curse (reverse of bless), protection from good; hold person, silence 15’ radius.

2-8 Set cultists (see new monsters) (33% chance): SZ M; AL LE; AC 9; MV 90’; HD 1; HP 7, 6, 6, 5, 5, 4, 4, 3; #AT 1; Dmg 1-4 (dagger) or 2-7 (flail) or 1-6 (staff). Special attacks: fanaticism. Possessions: padded armor; daggers; flails or staves.

### 4-129: Lounge

* This is a lounge area for cultists from the surrounding dormitories.
	* A wide fireplace vents to a cavern somewhere above.
		* The cultists are chronically short of firewood, so only 20% chance it is lit.
		* On a nail a foot up the interior of the chimney is a ring of water breathing (new) and a ring of warmth; they are blackened by smoke, but otherwise perfectly functional.
	* The chamber is austere, with several plank tables and benches, a water barrel, and only 6 comfortable-looking easy chairs, arranged in front of the fireplace.
* 50% chance one of the groups of cultists present in the dormitories will be here, talking, plotting, playing cards, and possibly torturing a slave or captive. 

### 4-130: Guard Post

* 2 Set guardsmen are posted to prevent inquisitive cultists venturing into the necropolis.
	* They lounge, bored, on a bench.
	* The locked door on the east wall is newly repaired. The guardsmen carry the key.

2 Set guardsmen (see new monsters), as 2nd-level Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 15, 12; #AT 1, Dmg 2-7 (mace), 1-6 (spear) and 1-4 (light crossbow). Special defense: fanaticism. Possessions: red scale mail and wooden shield; footman’s maces; spears; light crossbows with 20 bolts; key to the door on the east.

* See description at 4-125.

### 4-133: Cultists’ Rest

### 4-134: Larder

* This storeroom (locked) functions as the larder for the visiting cultists.
	* The main cult does not supply food, so groups of visitors bring their own, and deposit it here (quantities of boxes, bags, and bottles present depends on how many groups are currently visiting).
	* Supplies possibly present: skins of water and wine, packages of hard-tack, dried meat, dried fruit, even some fresh vegetables (worth their weight in gold!).
* There is a 25% chance that Jasper is asleep here on a simple pallet.

(25%) Jasper Roe, male Thorcin cook: for stats, see 4-135.
* Storeroom key.

### 4-135: Kitchen and Lounge

* This large room functions as a kitchen, dining area and lounge for cultists visiting the temple and Forum of Set.
	* A larger-than-normal tripod of heating (new) stands in the southwest corner.
	* The cook, Jasper Roe, has a small but effective array of cooking pots and utensils, as well as a preparation table along the south wall.
	* North of the fire is a pair of long trestle tables.
	* North and east of the room are comfortable stuffed chairs and low tables.
		* Scattered around them are a few religious pamphlets on parchment scrolls.
* Jasper is present 75% of the time, preparing food for the cultists.
* 50% chance a group of Set cultists are here, eating or hanging around.

Jasper Roe, male Thorcin cook (75%): SZ M; AL LE; AC 9; MV 120’; HD 1-1; #AT 1; Dmg 1-4 (cleaver). Possessions: cleaver and key to 4-134.

6-9 Set cultists (see new monsters) (50% chance): SZ M; AL LE; AC 9; MV 90’; HD 1; HP 7, 6, 6, 5, 5, 4, 4, 3, 3; #AT 1; Dmg 1-4 (dagger) or 2-7 (flail) or 1-6 (staff). Special attacks: fanaticism. Possessions: padded armor; daggers; flails or staves.

## Level 4: 136 - 146: Necropolis of Set

* These areas comprise the ancient necropolis of the cult of Set.
	* The areas were lost due to the collapse in antiquity of certain key tunnels (e.g., 4-137) until High Priestess Stephania ordered the stairs and tunnels cleared to allow the restoration of the necropolis.
	* Unfortunately, the priests found the necropolis was highly dangerous, inhabited by numerous undead under the domination of Meskenit the mummy (4-139c).
		* The entire area is so flooded with negative energy that turning undead is impossible.
		* Stephania tried to lure the intelligent undead out of their necropolis, but they know she intends to dominate them and did not fall for her ruse.
			* Stephania is unaware of the powers of the golden ankh in 4-138a, which would allow her to dominate the undead in the necropolis area.
	* The entire area is covered with dust and cobwebs, and the stonework is crumbling in numerous locations.  Unless otherwise indicated, the chambers are dark.

### 4-136: Dead Bodies!

* This chamber marks the limit of the modern Set cult’s expansion into the necropolis area.
	* The cult cleared it of debris, revealing some faded but still impressive murals on the south and west walls depicting the judgment of the dead.
		* From the southeast corner: a parade of dead souls; Anubis with the ankh of life leading an old-style Archontean man past several monstrous beings; the deceased confessing the status of his soul, with the phrase “I am strong, but Set is stronger” repeated numerous times in a Mithric word-cloud above his head; Maat weighing the heart against her feather; and Set recording the name of the deceased in a huge red scroll.
			* Experts in Mithric theology will note two deviations from the usual iconography of the judgment of the Dead: 1) normally the confession is “I am pure”, not “I am strong” with the addition of “but Set is stronger,” 2) normally Thoth is the recorder of the names of the dead, not Set. 
	* Numerous excavation tools lie about (picks, mauls, shovels, heavy canvas bags for toting rock, carrying straps, etc) and the gnawed corpses of eight workers slain by the undead from within the necropolis.
		* One turn after the chamber is entered, the eight corpses rise as strong zombies to smite intruders.
	* The tunnel to the east has been recently excavated; its walls are still rough, and the floor littered with rock dust and loose debris.
		* The ceiling is obviously unstable, propped up with sturdy wooden beams.

8 strong zombies: SZ M; AL N; AC 8; MV 60’; HD 3; HP 22, 20, 19, 19, 18, 18, 17, 16; #AT 1; Dmg 1-8. Special: always strike last.

### 4-137: Trapped Hallway

* Stairs at the north and south ends of this crumbling hallway lead down into the main areas of the necropolis.
	* The granite stairs are carved in a deliberately rough way, with steep risers, emphasizing the primal nature of death.
	* Two traps are located at the landing leading to 4-136:
		* Glyph of warding: placed by Stephania to fend off the lesser undead, it explodes for 20 HP fire damage. 
		* Unstable ceiling: significant noise (such as the glyph exploding) may (75%) cause a serious cave-in (those within 25’ save or take 3d8 damage).
			* Moderate noise, such as combat on the landing, has a 33% chance per turn of causing the collapse.

### 4-138: Eastern Crypt

* The ceiling of this huge chamber rises 20’ above the floor of the entrance hallway.
	* The crypt is completely lightless and as quiet as a tomb.
	* Two T-shaped platforms occupy either end of the crypt (4-138a and 4-13c), joined by an 80’ sunken walkway (15' below the platforms) lined with burial niches (4-138b).
		* Each platform holds 20 large stone sarcophagi carved in ornate, ancient style.
		* A 15’-tall statue of Set (as Set animal-headed) stands on western platform facing the entrance to the crypt.
		* The walls of the platforms were once painted with bright images of Set, the judgment of the dead, and the defeat of various enemies; mostly faded or flaked off now, with only some fragments visible.
* A band of corporeal undead dominated by the greater mum-my, Meskenit (see 4-139c), inhabit the crypt.
	* These stealthily approach any intruders within 2-6 rounds of the crypt being entered and attempt either to overwhelm the intruders or to drive them towards their master in 4-139c.

##### 4-138a: Entry Platform and Statue of Set

* The entry platform holds 20 sealed sarcophagi (for potential contents see 4-138c) and an imposing statue of Set in the form of the Set animal.
	* The statue of Set is black obsidian with a white marble head, ears and snout of solid gold, and lapis eyes (the head is worth 4,575 gp, 340 lb).
	* He holds a 24”-long golden ankh (new) in one hand and a 3’-long silver flail with many heads in the other (the sterling flail of Set, new).
	* On the right calf of the statue, about 3’ from the floor, are two flattened patches of obsidian (spot as secret door, unless specifically examining the whole statue).
		* The upper patch has four 1” squares, each with a different rune carved in it
		* The lower one features four empty 1” squares arranged in a cruciform style.
	* The statue can be manipulated in various ways to produce effects, and it may activate in response to actions.

The following actions might awaken Set Statue:
1. Opening any sealed sarcophagi: the statue activates as a stone golem to smite desecrators using its ankh, flail, and magical powers. It pursues intruders within the crypt, but will not leave it.
2. Supplicating Set by stating, “I am strong, but Set is stronger” (c.f. 4-136): this awakens the Set golem; its eyes shift from blue to a menacing, glowing red.  The golem intervenes against any who assault the supplicants, including undead.
3. Breaking open the burial niches: 5% cumultive chance per niche that the Set golem activates to smite the intruders.
4. Attempting to steal the silver flail: see below for when/if this might awaken the golem.

Manipulating the statue may also produce effects:
1. Removing the gold snout or ears, or the lapis eyes: blasts of blue energy unerringly strike the desecrator for 6d6 damage (save vs spells for half).
2. Removing the golden ankh: the golden ankh (new) can be removed.
	* It can be picked up by those of any alignment, but only serves those who are neutral or evil; it acts as a cursed object for those of good alignment.
	* Within the necropolis of Set, wielded by a neutral or evil character, the ankh turns undead as if it were a 12th-level cleric.
	* For other powers of the ankh, see new magic items. 
3. Removing the silver flail: the flail (new) can only be safely removed by a non-good handler who specifically invokes Set by name and (briefly) explains his need.  Otherwise the statue animates and attacks.
4. Manipulating the runes and empty squares: together they form a puzzle
	* Touching a rune and then an empty square causes that rune to appear in the square in tiny, fiery script.  Touching a square again clears it.
	* The runes are: ankh (protection); djed column (strength/body); was stick (power); and lotus (creation).
	* The four squares are in a diamond pattern (1 through 4, clockwise from the top).
	* Each effect can only be produced 1x/week, and certain effects (e.g. ankh-ankh-ankh-djed) are only possible once per person.

* Ankh Ankh Ankh Ankh
	* Antimagic shell around manipulator of runes, lasts 3-6 weeks. No magic in or out. Manipulator’s body glows with magical yellow light, visible 60’ away.
* Ankh Ankh Ankh Djed
	* +1 CON, permanent
* Djed Djed Djed Djed
	* Body overloads. An extremity withers and becomes useless [1=left hand, 2=right hand, 3=left arm, 4=right arm, 5=left leg, 6=left foot, 7=right leg, 8=right foot].
* Was Was Was Lotus
	* Manipulator must discharge ray of power (2-8 damage) every hour for the next 1-4 days. If no enemies, friends or self are/is affected.
* Lotus Ankh Ankh Lotus
	* Protection from undead cast on manipulator. Lasts 2-5 days; AC +2 vs undead; undead do -2 damage; saves are at +2 versus undead effects.
* Lotus Ankh Ankh Djed
	* The following spells are cast on all within 10’ radius: heal, neutralize poison, cure disease.
* Was Was Was Was
	* Magical short-circuit, 2-5 magic items closest to statue are drained of power. Save at -2 to avoid.
* Lotus Lotus Lotus Lotus
	* Chaotic effect (see table below).
* Was Lotus Lotus Ankh
	* Makes manipulator’s chief weapon +2 for 2 weeks.
* Lotus Djed Djed Lotus
	* Creates 4 ghouls who attack immediately; they cannot be turned.
* Djed Djed Djed Was
	* One of sarcophagi bursts open. 50% chance wight emerges. 
	* Roll on sarcophagus table for contents.
	* D10 Chaotic Effect
* Lotus Ankh Djed Was
	* d6 zap
* The GM can create other combinations of runes if she wishes.
* Other combinations
	* Deliver a sharp pulse of magical energy for 1d6 damage to the manipulator.

Chaotic Effects

1
Manipulator grows demonic body part (horn, tail, extra eye, differently colored eyes, etc.), CHA +1 to all evil alignments.

2 Summons 4-6 berserkers who fight for manipulator or 6 hours.

3
Summons 1-3 Type 1 demons; they fight opponents of the manipulator unless none are present, in which case they attack the manipulator.

4
Monster Magnet: double chances of Random Encounters for 3-6 days.

5
Treasure Nose: can sniff out treasure worth at least 100 gp from 150 feet; lasts 3 days.

6
Opens portal to lower plane; portal stays open for 6 days. 25% chance per day that 1-2 inhabitants of that lower plane emerge.

7
Magnetizes Set Statue: all metal in 20’ radius attaches itself to statue with unbreakable force. Lasts 3-6 days. Magic metal gets a save.

8
Repulsor: a wall of force drops across entrance to crypt. Lasts 3 days.

9
A floor paver is vaporized, revealing stairs leading down. They lead 1-2= to a sub-level, 3-4=to the Astral Plane, 5-6=to an alternate world.

10
A random attribute increases by 1.


1 Set golem, aka stone golem: SZ L; AL N; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 14; HP 60; #AT 1; Dmg 3-24. Special attacks: slow once every other round. Special defenses: +2 or better weapons to hit; immune to most magic.

##### 4-138c: Rear Platform and Sarcophagi

* The sarcophagi here are ancient, and elaborately carved with representative half-round carvings of themes of Set, dungeon exploration, monster slaughter, and crueler themes.
	* They vary in height, length and width (averaging 6’ long, 3’ wide, and 4’ high).
	* All are sealed (breaking a seal requires 1d4 rounds and a combined STR of 36).
	* Opening any sarcophagus awakens the Set golem (see 4-138a).
	* The contents of any sarcophagus are determined randomly:
* A band of undead led by a wight clusters here among the sarcophagi.
	* Within 6 rounds of intruders entering the crypt, they begin to creep along the walkway (4-138b), hoping to take the intruders by surprise as they inspect 4-138a.

### 4-139: Southern Crypt 

* This immense chamber is broadly similar to its companion at 4-138.
	* Its ceiling rises 20’ above the floor.
	* Two T-shaped platforms occupy either end of the crypt (4-139a and 4-139c) joined by an 80’-long sunken walkway lined with burial niches (4-139b).
		* The walkway is 15’ below the floor of the two platforms.
		* Each platform holds 20 large stone sarcophagi carved in ornate, ancient style.
		* A large statue of Set once stood on the platform of 4-139Aa but now lies in pieces among the sarcophagi.
		* The walls of the platforms are painted with bright images of Set, the Judgment of the Dead, and the defeat of various enemies.
* Meskenit the greater mummy rules the necropolis area from this crypt.
	* He is often found at 4-139c, accompanied by a lesser mummy and a pack of ghasts; if not there, he will be in 4-146.

##### 4-139a: Front Platform and Statue of Set

* The entry platform features 20 sarcophagi and the ruined statue of Set.
	* The obsidian statue of Set lies in pieces; only the feet remain on the pedestal.
		* Trap (glyph of warding): Meskenit placed a glyph (18 fire damage) on top of the ruined pedestal of the statue.
	* Set’s white marble head, complete with gold snout and ears and lapis eyes, has rolled behind one of the sarcophagi (4,575 gp, 340 lbs).
		* If approached, the lapis eyes pulse with a sinister blue light, but in its ruined state Set cannot act through this golem any longer.
		* Set used to carry a 24” golden ankh and a 3’ golden scepter, but Meskenit has stolen these objects (see 4-146). 
	* These sarcophagi are ancient and elaborately carved, with half-round carvings of Set, dungeon exploration, monster slaughter, and crueler themes.
		* The sarcophagi vary in height, length and width (averaging 6’ long, 3’ wide, and 4’ high), and are all closed and sealed.
			* Breaking a seal requires 1d4 rounds and a total 36 strength.
			* For the contents of any sarcophagus, see tables at 4-138c.
* Initially, there are no opponents here.  Meskenit and his minions prefer to rest at 4-139c (see tactics therein).

##### 4-139b: Walkway and Burial Niches

* Each 10’ section of wall along the walkway between the platforms contains 9 burial niches.
	* Thus 252 niches per wall, 504 niches in total.
	* The plugs of fifteen of the niches have burst open from within.
	* The remainder are sealed, and contain skeletal remains plus 1-2 objects from the relevant table located at 4-138b.
* Halfway down the walkway between the platforms, Meskenit placed a glyph of warding (paralysis).

##### 4-139c: Rear Platform and Sarcophagi

* The rear platform holds 20 more sarcophagi (on average 6’ long, 3’ wide, and 4’ high).
	* They are ancient and elaborately carved with themes of Set, dungeon exploration, monster slaughter, and crueler themes.
	* Three sarcophagi on this platform have been opened.
		* Their contents are available (see tables in 4-138c).
	* Breaking a sarcophagus seal requires 1d4 rounds and a total 36 strength.
	* For the contents of any sarcophagus, see tables at 4-138c.
* Meskenit is usually present here, accompanied by his lesser mummy and pack of ghasts.
	* They wait quietly, hoping that the glyphs at 4-139a and 4-139b will weaken and immobilize invading PCs.
		* When the second trap has been tripped (or negated), Meskenit releases the pack of ghasts and orders his lieutenant into the fray.
		* He remains on the platform, casting spells, all the while intoning vile charms and curses in a dry, raspy, high-pitched voice.

Meskenit, a greater mummy (see new monsters): SZ M; AL LE; AC 0; MV 90’; HD 10+3; HP 73; #AT 1; Dmg 2-12; MR 50%. Special attacks: aura of despair (saves at -3); mummy rot; command other undead. Special defenses: magic weapons to hit (+1 does 1 HP damage; +2 does half damage; +3 does full damage); immune to cold; takes half damage from non-magical fire; turned as a ghost.
* Possessions: 
	* a brooch of shielding (61 HP left)
	* a pair of bracers of haste (+10' move, haste for 5-20 rounds aging 1 year)
	* a staff of the necromancer (24/25 charges)
		* 0 charges: prot good, detect good, detect magic
		* 1 charge: curse, dispel magic, fear, animate dead
		* 3 charges: cacodemon, death spell
* Spells as 11th-level cleric with WIS 18 (7/6/5/4/2/1)
	* curse, command, cause light wounds (x3), protection from good, darkness
	* chant, hold person (x2), resist fire (x2), silence 15’ radius
	* animate dead, blindness, dispel magic (x2), glyph of warding
	* cause serious wounds (x2), poison, X protection from good 10’ radius
	* X flame strike, true seeing; blade barrier

8 ghasts: SZ M; AL CE; AC 4; MV 150’; HD 4; HP 30, 27, 25, 23, 22, 21, 20, 19, 18; #AT 3; Dmg 1-4/1-4/1-8. Special attacks: stench (10' radius, vs poison or -2 attack); paralysis. Special defenses: immune to sleep and charm.
