12 - 0 / 18
### 4-140: Storage Room

* This low-ceilinged room (8’ tall) and was a general storage room for the necropolis.
	* The walls are undecorated and roughly hewn.
	* Three heavy sarcophagus bottoms (no lids) line the center of the room.
		* One has partial half-round carvings; the others are still rough.
	* A stone bench is set against the south wall, on which are numerous stone carving tools, some jars of spices (2-200 gp) and (dried) unguents, and a large bundle of linen wrappings.
	* Secret Door (north, into narrow hallway): narrow and small (5’x5’), easy (1 in 4) to locate.  Opened by force or by rapping on it three times in rapid succession.
	* Secret Door (north, to 4-149): small (5’x5’). Opened by pressing a dime-sized button inset on one of the stair risers.
	* Secret Door (south, to 4-141): quite wide (8’) and short (4’ tall), hard to detect (1 in 8). Opened by sliding a thin knife into the bottom seam to release a catch, after which the bottom may be pushed inward.
* Noise and time spent here likely attracts the ghouls and wight from 4-138c.

### 4-141: Lost Altar

* A rough stone altar rests against the south wall, coated in dried blood and strongly radiating evil.
	* It is an illusion concealing the secret door behind it.
		* If believed, the viewer feels that a great evil lurks here, or the arrival of demonic evil is imminent, and retreat is the best action.
		* If disbelieved, the secret door is readily apparent on the south wall.
* Secret Door (south): 2’ wide and 5’ tall.  Difficult to locate unless the illusion is overcome, then normal.  Pressing a stud near the floor activates the door, which snaps inward on spring-loaded hinges.

### 4-142: Tomb of Theskelon the High Priest

* This ancient tomb holds the remains of Theskelon, the high priest of Set responsible for the creation of the necropolis.
	* The current Set priests are ignorant of the existence of this tomb.
	* Discovery of Theskelon’s tomb would be of signal importance to the modern cult.
		* Those who report it to Stephania receive 500 gp each.
		* Looting the tomb provokes the cult's eternal enmity, should it become known.

* Theskelon’s tomb is decorated with a stark white plaster, on which are painted a number of unusual frescoes (intact, if a little faded).
	* The collage-like images are impressive, yet simultaneously amateurish; they are also fairly chilling, since all four connote violence and savagery. 
		* 1) an enormous black boar with an 11” yellow sun clamped in its hairy jaws.
			* Some sort of lumpy substance has been used to outline the boar’s body and provide relief to the otherwise flat wall.
			* The boar’s one visible eye is a hole in the fresco, it's back painted red, but without a pupil.
			* Actual bristles and bits of horn were implanted in the plaster.
			* The ‘sun’ is an 11" sphere whose outer layer of painted plaster conceals a 10” solid gold center (400 gp).
		* 2) a crocodile devouring a heron
			* Realistic teeth are implanted into the bas-relief, and the heron-legs are made of femurs of some huge mammal.
		* 3) a huge Set animal squatting on a turtle
			* The eyes of the Set animal are 2”-diameter black crystals; the turtle’s shell is made out of an enormous turtle shell.
		* 4) a tall human figure dressed as a priest of Set with a garish, grinning white face splitting a huge baboon in half with an axe.
			* The features are particularly accentuated: the human’s head is bulbous, lumpy and features real black hair, the axe head is an actual axe head; the relief of the baboon is covered by bits of matted real fur.
	* In the middle of the chamber is the unusual ‘sarcophagus’ of Theskelon.
		* It is a single unbroken block of mottled green granite, 4’ wide, 8’ long, and 6’ tall, obviously not native to the surrounding stone.
		* Inspection reveals no anomalies, fissures, or cracks.
		* A continuous inscription at a height of 4’ reads (Mithric) “Theskelon is in me. I am in Theskelon”
		* There is a spherical depression on the top of the block, 10” in diameter.
			* Incised around this depression in tiny letters “Let Set devour the rays of his old rival.”
			* If the gold sun is removed from the wall and placed in this depression, it melts and the granite block crumbles to dust and debris (2d10 under DEX to avoid 1d4 from flying shards), revealing the inner sarcophagus.
				* A gleaming gold and lapis sarcophagus (600 gp worth of materials), sculpted as a recumbent man with crossed arms, dressed in ceremonial Set robes.
					* It is trapped with explosive runes.

Obtaining the Orb
* It's not obvious there is something below the plaster.
* The plaster around the orb is rock hard.  Smashing it free has a 50% chance of deforming the orb into uselessness.
* Inserting the missing ruby (not glass) eye into the boar causes the plaster to crumble, releasing the orb.

Obtaining the Eye
* The clue to the location of the missing eye is a pun in the inscription on the sarcophagus.
	* “I am in Theskelon”: the missing ‘eye’ is buried inside the plaster bas-relief of the Theskelon image (i.e., “I” or Theskelon).
	* Digging around in the image’s bulbous head rewards two red gems, each 2” in diameter: a ruby eye (the real eye, 1000 gp) and a piece of glass.

Inside the Sacrophagus
* The inert bones of Theskelon
* Several important artifacts of the ancient cult of Set.
	* Not magical or inherently valuable; they hold clues to exploration of the dungeon ruins. To the current cult of Set, as symbolic and historical artifacts they are priceless.
		* Signet Ring of Theskelon
			* A gold ring (50 gp) with carved image of a male head and the legend “Theskelon the Master.”
			* As a symbol of legitimacy within the priesthood of Set, this ring would be of incalculable value to High Priestess Stephania.
			* Note: this is not a true ring of Set, as it predates them.
		* Plaques of the Beacon
			* Three copper plaques 10” wide by 14” tall hold incised schematic drawings of three of the modules from the Beacon.
			* One side of each plaque shows the complete floorplan of the given module (both levels, if the module has two levels), along with one or two Rudishva glyphs. The reverse side has some instructions in Mithric.
				* The first plaque depicts the engine room of the Beacon (7-143). The glyphs are for ‘power’ and ‘flight’.  The notes read “Unknown location. Possibly near the administrative center and shrines. Likely a powerful weapon.”
				* The second plaque depicts the crew quarters (6-112), with the glyphs ‘dwelling’ and ‘peaceful’; the notes read “the Scriptor claims to know its location, as his workmen found it. But the workmen were devoured and the Scriptor is not talking.”
					* GM: refers to Lucius Cornelius Scriptor and the construction of his tomb (6-130 to 6-135) at a location near to the crew pod.
				* The third plaque depicts the weapons locker (6-27) and uses the glyphs ‘armory’ and ‘mechanical voice’; the notes read “Unknown location. Reference to a voice is undoubtedly a mistake.”
					* GM: the voice refers to the AI, RAJ-750 (6-27).
		* The Rise of the Sortians
			* An unusual set of bone plates containing text (secret tongue of the priests of Set) (books).
		* The Theskelonia
			* A parchment codex with black hide covers (books).
		* An ivory plaque with the last third of the treatise Preparing for the Long Death (books, 3000 gp).
			* Contains the new spell, the long death, and some necromantic theory.
			* The other two plaques are in the possession of Meskenit (4-146).
		* A key that fits the lock in the stone door at SL8-1.

### 4-143: Slaver’s Rest

* A former necropolis antechamber cut off from the rest of the area by ancient cave-ins.
	* Used as a way station by the Guild of Service when traveling the Long Stair (4-19).
		* A couple of benches, a water barrel, a set of broken shackles, and a coiled whip are scattered about the floor.
		* 4 guildsmen from the Guild of Service stand guard here, ensuring nothing dangerous emerges from 4-154.  A brass horn hangs from the wall, used to  alert those in 4-19 of any threat.
	* The door to the west is stuck.
		* It leads to stairs that once connected to 4-145, but that now end in a cave-in.
			* Harold the Wary, a lost adventurer, is cowering in the broken hallway behind the stuck door.
				* He took refuge here during a change in the guard rotation, and is increasingly desperate to make his way past the guards.

* Harold is a big man, but a bit of a coward (‘wary’, as he calls it).
	* He was part of the gang led by Gillen the magic user (see 4-180), but deserted when Gillen revealed his intention to set up operations as a bandit.
	* He fled north and east, and barely managing to avoid capture by the slavers. 
	* He could retrace his footsteps to 4-179 and would happily warn new comrades of the threat posed by Gillen and Co. if those new comrades promised to help him escape the Halls.
	* He has never visited the Forum (4-2).
	* Unless convinced that he does possess courage by some friendly, good-aligned persons, Harold like to quaffs his potion and disappears at the first sign of danger.

Harold the Wary, 3rd-level male Archontean fighter: SZ M; AL LN; AC 5; MV 60’; HD 3; HP 22; #AT 1; Dmg 3-8 (footman’s mace) or 1-4 (crossbow bolt). Abilities: STR 16, INT 15, WIS 9, 
DEX 10, CON 13, CHA 15. Possessions: scale mail and shield; footman’s mace; a light crossbow with 12 bolts; a pouch of marbles; a purse with 39 sp; and a potion of invisibility.

4 guildsmen, as 2nd-level male Archontean fighters: SZ M; AL LE; AC 8; MV 120’; HD 2; HP 18, 17, 16, 15; #AT 1; Dmg 2-7 (spears, clubs). Possessions: leather armor; spears; and clubs. Special: they have +1 to damage from STR.

### 4-144: Guardian Noses

* This chamber offers another resting point for those traveling the Long Stair (4-19).
	* The east and west walls are painted with identical enchanted frescoes of an enormous, bulbous human or humanoid nose, complete with pores and follicles.
	* They ‘smell’ (detect) alignment, and bray loudly if they sense a non-evil alignment.
		* This provokes an immediate random encounter roll (the encounter won't be surprised thanks to the noice).
	* Two gallons of liquid and some cloth can easily remove the frescoes.

### 4-145: Broken Corridor

* This long corridor extending east from 4-148 (under 4-145 and 4-139b) is filled with dust and cobwebs.
	* At the east end, motion has a 25% chance / Turn to cause a cave-in affecting the final 40’ of the corridor (3d8 under DEX or 4d6 damage).

### 4-146: Lair of the Mummy Lord

* Meskenit the greater mummy (4-139c) has made this undecorated chamber his war room, to plot vengeance against the living and to run experiments in mummy creation.
	* This chamber was a preparation room for the necropolis, and is filled with appropriate gear: hammers and chisels, a wooden work table with jars of unguents and preserving spices, two boxes filled with wrapping linen, a dozen sheets of thinly hammered gold leaf (12 gp each), and a clay pot filled with bits of odd-sized lapis (a total of 230 gp).
	* In an iron box on the worktable are a pair of ivory plaques inscribed with an ancient treatise entitled “Preparing for the Long Death.” (books) (creation of mummies)
		* The first plaque describes the materials needed for mummification; the second plaque has the process and initial spells needed to accomplish this rite.
		* Meskenit doesn’t know that he is missing a third plaque (see 4-142), which explains his frustrating results to date.
	* Meskenit keeps his treasure piled under the worktable.
		* The golden ankh (24”, 2500 gp) and scepter (3’, 3500 gp) taken from the broken Set statue at 4-139a.
		* 2 3’-tall, solid gold statuettes of Set in boar form (2,500 gp each)
		* 12 carved alabaster canopic jars inset with jet and lapis, each showing one of the Twelve (375 gp each)
		* A set of solid silver embalming tools (75 gp)
		* A broken string of 25 fine pearls, in a clay jar (3,000 gp)
		* 2 teeth of Pol (new)
		* six cones of rare incense (75 gp each), a cone of incense of relaxation (new)
		* a silk bag filled with 3 doses of dust of disappearance
		* a potion of clarity (new)
		* a pair of slippers of stealth (new); an ankh of healing (new); a bardiche +4; a suit of abyssal armor (new)
		* a scroll with the Liturgy of the Strong (books)
		* 2 scrolls of protection from undead; a scroll of curse item (new).
	* Four unfinished sarcophagi lean against the north wall.
		* The pathetic results of two of Meskenit's mummy creation efforts are stuffed in one of the unfinished sarcophagi.
	* A finished sarcophagi is bound tightly with iron chains.
		* Meskenit created an aberrant ‘good mummy’ named Icthelon, and locked it  in the finished sarcophagus for later study.
			* It beats and scratches at the lid if it detects good creatures in the chamber. 
			* The corpse which Meskenit used to create his mummy was that of the lawful good priest Icthelon.  Thoth ensured that the product remains sentient and good.
			* If Icthelon is released and is not attacked, he might aid good-aligned PCs with information and physical assistance, perhaps accompanying them throughout the upper parts of the complex.
			* He has good knowledge of the layouts of the public areas devoted to Set and Thoth, although no knowledge of current inhabitants.
	* Secret Door (south): 2’ wide by 4’ high, difficult (1 in 8) to spot.
		* Pressing a 2”-square pressure plate on the floor opens the door.
		* None of the mummies know of this door.

Icthelon the good mummy (see new monsters): SZ M; AL LG; AC 3; MV 60’; HD 6+3; HP 41; #AT 1; Dmg 1-12. Special attacks: divine touch (cures 1-8 HP to good creatures, inflicts 1-8 HP damage on evil). Special defenses: +1 or better weapons to hit; magic weapons do half damage; immune to sleep, hold, charm, poison, and paralysis.

## Level 4: 147 - 165

### 4-147: Unfinished Preparation Room

* This chamber is roughly hewn and unfinished.
	* A 2’ x 2’ table is set in the middle, on which is a copper bowl filled with mercury, in which float two disembodied eyes (eyes of Pol, new).
		* They react to light (dilating, etc.) and follow movement.
	* Secret Door (west): easy to find (1 in 4), opens by pulling outward into the room.

##### 4-147a: Connecting Hall

* This dusty hallway leads to a stair that descends to the hallway (4-145) leading to 4-148.
	* Secret Door (north): opens by pushing inward on the 3’ x 6’ panel.
		* It leads to a narrow tunnel that ends at the chasm in a concealed door, beyond which is the invisible bridge to 4-127.
			* Note: the bridge will only be present if the levers have been manipulated appropriately at 4-127.

### 4-148: Hidden Mortuary Temple

* Knowledge of this mortuary temple has been lost to the Set Cult for over 1,200 years.
	* Originally it served as a lesser temple, where the remains of donors could be prepared and those donors’ service to Set celebrated.
* A raised walkway overlooks the main temple.
	* Steep stairs lead down 15’ feet to the floor below.  
	* The temple is dark and radiates evil.
	* Frescoes decorate the north, west, and eat walls.
		* (north) pastoral scenes involving wildlife, and especially black boars.
		* (west and east) painted in a trompe l’oeil technique to give the impression of crypts extending off into the distance. 
	* The south wall has a colossal, 20’ statue of Set in half relief.
		* Set’s arms extend outward to form a canopy over the altar some 10’ below.
			* Within the altar, behind metal bars is the skull of Gneis Valor (new).
		* The statue is stone, but brightly painted (flesh a coppery brown, the headdress and loincloth are white with blue and yellow highlights).
		* The statue’s eyes are deceptively gem-like (colored glass, worthless).
	* Four slim black pillars rise to a barrel-vaulted ceiling.
		* A cluster of five human-sized shapes is huddled around a 3’-tall cylinder within the area circumscribed by the four pillars.
			* The cylinder radiates good, it is a salt lamp of protection (greater) (new).
			* The shapes are remains of an adventuring team.  When ambushed by shadows, they used the lamp to drive off the creatures.  Lacking fuel, the party mage desperately used her own life force to power it.  When she grew exhausted, the lamp failed, and the shadows massacred the party.
				* Only a small residue of red ‘wax’ remains in the lamp.
			* On the adventurers:
				* suits of banded mail, chain mail, splint mail and leather armor +2; a broadsword, footman’s flail, a short bow, and 3 daggers; 78 gp, 120 sp, a 130 gp gem, a 90 gp gem, an oriental carpet showing the 3rd mystery of Set (375 gp), 2 vials of acid, a short sword +1, 10 arrows +2, a wand of magic missiles (1 charge), a cursed wand of life-stealing (27 charges) (new), potions (fire resistance, animal control), a ring of higher purpose (new), a lesser power supply (empty).
* The shadows in this chamber take 5-7 rounds to notice intruders and gather for the attack, using gang tactics to bring down one opponent at a time.

2 greater shadows (see new monsters): SZ M; AL CE; AC 5; MV 120’; HD 5+1; HP 36, 30; #AT 1; Dmg 2-12. Special attacks: ability drain. Special defenses: +1 or better weapons to hit; immune to cold, poison, paralysis, sleep, charm, and hold; turned as a wraith.

14 shadows: SZ M; AL CE; AC 7; MV 120; HD 3+3; HP 24, 22, 21, 20, 19, 18, 18, 17; #AT 1; Dmg 2-5. Special attacks: STR drain. Special defenses: 90% undetectable; +1 or better weapons to hit; immune to sleep, charm, hold, and cold. 

The magic user’s spell book: charm person, comprehend languages, detect magic, feather fall, floating disk, hold portal, magic missile, push, read magic, sleep, unseen servant; detect evil, ESP, fool’s gold, knock, mirror image, ray of enfeeblement, shatter, web; blink, clairvoyance, hold person, infravision, monster summoning I, protection from normal missiles, slow, suggestion, water breathing, wind wall; charm monster, enchanted weapon, fumble, remove curse.

### 4-149: Punishment Square

* A former crossroads on the Long Stair (4-19), this area is used by the Guild of Service  to intimidate new slaves arriving at the pits.
	* Four torches light the area.
	* To the east, by the door, is a large barrel of torches and pitch.
	* On the western side of the square, by the caved-in corridor, the slavers have erected two frames on which they display the bloodied bodies of troublesome slaves.
	* Secret Door (west): 5’x5’, no opening mechanism from this side (50 HP; AC 0 to smash). Inside is a short set of stairs leads upward to 4-140.
	* Secret Door (southwest, into 4-140): 5’x5’, easy to locate (1 in 4).  It must be pulled inward, difficult to get enough grip to do so).

* Currently a Wiskin fighter and a stoic Archontean ranger are hanging on the frames.
	* Neither has any equipment.
	* The ranger is in bad shape, the slavers amputated his hands and is unlikely to last much longer.
		* He stoically whispers a few words of advice about the complex to any who aid him in his final agonies.
	* Hjalti the Wiskin is in better shape; though badly burned and branded (down to 6 HP), he could be revived.
		* He was taken by the Guild of Service while exploring the southern great cavern (3-172) as part of a failed adventuring expedition.
		* Hjalti knew that the (now-dead) party leader wished to locate a certain ‘evil sorcerer’ named Kerbog Khan (SL12-25), who was ‘wanted by all the collegia, and especially the Collegium of Macrina,’ for theft of valuable treatises, codices, and alchemical materials.
		* They also had rumors of a 'lord of the fungi', and were searching the fungal forest to locate them (Note: he means the false-Ptarmis at 3-176).
		* Hjalti was in the slave pits (4-11), but was punished for trying to lead an escape.
		* He happily offer directions to those who aid him, and could navigate the route from 4-149 to 4-163, 4-160, 4-159, 3-212A, 3-172 and eventually to the cliff exit at 3-189.

Kiglon, 3rd-level male Archontean ranger: SZ M; AL CG; AC 10; MV 120’; HD 3; HP 1 (max 32); #AT 1; Dmg by weapon. Abilities: STR 14, INT 13, WIS 15, DEX 10, CON 17, CHA 9. Kiglon will die in 1-3 turns unless cured.

Hjalti, 4th-level male Wiskin fighter: SZ M; AL CN; AC 10; MV 120’; HD 4; HP 6 (max 47); #AT 1; Dmg by weapon. Abilities: STR 17, INT 8, WIS 10, DEX 12, CON 18, CHA 14.

### 4-150: Empty Antechamber

* Faded frescoes depict the preparation of the dead for burial.
	* The passage south collapsed in antiquity (digging 1d4 turns produces a troll thegn’s passport (av items).
* The door east has been recently refurbished and oiled, and is locked.
	* The key is held by the duty guardsmen in 4-17.

### 4-151: Cavern of Bones

* The passage from the west leads to a ledge overlooking an enormous cavern.
	* 20' below the ledge, a layer of bones covers the floor.
		* The layer is extremely deep; the floor of the cavern is 75’ below the ledge.
			* The ancient cult of Set tossed unwanted corpses here, including of lesser believers (who usually imagined a more noble burial in the necropolis).
			* Recently, the Guild of Service began disposing of casualties here, so the bodies closest to the ledge are fresh (some not yet skeletonized).
		* Those foolishly pawing around in the remains may catch a disease from filth and tiny vermin devouring the flesh of corpses (25% + 5% per turn).
	* An exit leading to 4-53 exists to the southwest, 50’ below the entry ledge and 25’ above the floor.

##### 4-151a: Pukel-Mander

* On another ledge 75’ above the floor of the pit of bones stands a loathsome pukel-mander (new).
	* Touching it with anything but a tear of Kauket (new) animates 8 heqeti hopping dead from the pit of bones.  If defeated, they can't reanimate for 2 hours.
	* It takes a round for them to clamber out of the mass of bones
* Secret Door (south): a 5’-diameter circular plug in the stone, opening if a tear of Kauket is placed in an oval indentation in the rock face (can be Knocked).

8 heqeti hopping dead (see new monsters): SZ M; AL CE; AC 5; MV 90’; HD 3; HP 22, 21, 20, 19, 19, 17, 16, 15; #AT 1; Dmg 1-8. Special attacks: leap; cursed tongue. Special defenses: turned as ghasts; half damage from piercing and edged weapons; immune to sleep, charm, hold, and cold-based spells.

### 4-152: Gate to the Abyss

* A spherical tunnel 6’ in diameter spirals downward 200' at a steep slope, its rough walls pebbled and oily, ending at a shimmering orange veil of energy.
	* Scrawled on the wall (secret tongue of Set): “Danger! None have returned.”
	* Stepping through the one-way veil brings the foolish to the 497th layer of abyss, ruled by Kauket.

Stone shaped closed
### 4-153: Arcanum Cave

* This cave is a natural geode of arcanum (new).
	* The walls, floor and ceiling of the cave pulsate with a sickly orange light.
	* Like all such pockets, it exerts a powerful compulsion on arcane casters. 
* The tunnel south enters the chasm (4-154) 10’ below the pavement at 4-154 and 4-155.

### 4-154: Ledge and Chasm

* The sturdy, iron-reinforced wood door in the western corridor is obviously new.
	* It has been spiked shut from the west.
* East of the door is a ledge of cracked and buckled blue-granite paving stones overlooking a small chasm.
	* Two iron torch brackets are embedded in the pavement near the chasm edge.
	* The long gone foundations of a bridge are visible.
	* A lone pillar by the chasm edge suggests that this chamber may once have been joined to 4-155.
	* The chasm descends 100’ below the ledge, narrowing to 10’, to a sump of clear water, and rises 50' above.
* The tunnel to 4-153 is 10’ below 4-154 and 4-155. 
* The chasm cephalopods here are slowly attracted to heat and movement, gathering to investigate in 1d3 Turns.

8 small chasm cephalopods (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 5; MV 60’ flying (Class A); HD 2; HP 15, 14, 13, 13, 12, 11, 10, 8; #AT 5 (4 tentacles and a beak); Dmg 1-3/1-3/1-3/1-3/1-4; 
MR 25%. Special attacks: surprise on 1-4.

### 4-155: Forgotten God

* Buckled blue-granite pavers line this shrine to a forgotten god.
	* The chamber is wreathed in heavy ropes of cobwebs.  Any decorations have long since faded.
	* The walls are the same grey-blue granite, with many of the sheathing slabs fallen, leaving the bare stone beneath.
	* Four heavy pillars of green granite rise to a flat ceiling 30’ above the pavement.
		* The pillar segments were carved with elaborate geometric and representational schemes, but the passage of time has worn most of the images smooth.
			* One might see a glimpse of a cylindrical entity with four legs, or some bipeds that look like insects (mantises); a few random humans are shown, though their dress and depiction is foreign and puzzling.
	* The paving stones are treacherous, and liable to collapse.
		* Walking carefully is safe, though the pavers roll and tilt underfoot.
		* Running or fighting has a 1 in 6 chance per person per 10’ square crossed (or fought on) of collapse (50% fall prone, 50% fall into a 10' hole for 1d6).
	* A colossal nataraja statue stands in front of the opening to 4-156, at the east end.
		* Buried under the paver directly in front of the statue is a box of grey plasteel.
			* Locked (-25% to pick) and trapped with electronic intruder repulsors.
				* The trap can be detected normally and disarmed normally.
					* Even successful disarming shocks for 2d6.
					* Disarming does ensure the damage isn't repeated, allowing picking (otherwise 2d6 shock per round touching the lockplate).
					* Contains: 6 plate-sized octagonal pieces of platinum (1500 gp each) and, wrapped in red silk, Troll-hammer, an enchanted mace (new).
		* It dances, standing on one foot, with arms fanning around its chest.
		* The hands are all broken off.
		* The head has the horns and smiling fanged mouth of a rudishva, face snarling with glaring eyes.
			* Inobviously, the statue’s four fangs are solid platinum (200 gp each).
			* Its features are cloaked in dust and cobwebs, and hard to make out.  If cleaned up, the statue has crisp, clean features in unlike the decrepitude of the rest of the shrine. 
			* Scraping away dust also reveals a niche in the statue’s chest, with a faintly glowing, fist-sized piece of orange arcanum (see new magic items) inside. 
				* If touched, the statue booms in several unknown languages, then Archontean, “Do not touch the heart of the God. This is your final warning.” 
				* If removed, it shouts in several languages, then Archontean “The Six shall be notified that the Uthric has been disrupted. Punishment commences!.”
					* Two type II demons gate in and attack the desecrators.
					* The statue begin casting (in order): slow, darkness 15’ radius, and cloudkill.
					* Behind the lump, within the chest niche, is a silver scroll case (scroll w/ glasseye, legend lore, and repulsion).

* Note: 25% chance the spiders of 4-156 are encountered here.  Will be attracted if combat breaks out with demons or chasm cephalopods.

2 type II demons: SZ L; AL CE; AC -2; MV 60’, 120’ swimming; HD 9; HP 64, 57; #AT 3; Dmg 1-3/1-3/4-16; MR 55%. Constant effect: infravision. Special attacks: cause fear. Special defenses: half damage from cold, electricity, fire, and gas. Special: darkness 15’ radius; levitate; detect invisible objects; telekinesis; gate (20% chance). 

### 4-156: Spider Lair

* The chamber is sheathed in polished black granite with rounded corners.
	* A clutch of huge spiders lairs here in a mass of webs, dust, and debris.
	* Amid the rubble are a few items.
		* Three of the hands from the statue in 4-155: one has an enchanted scimitar, one a non-magical mace, and one a platinum rod of authority (175 gp).
			* The scimitar is intelligent, and named Mistral (new).
		* A copper slate inscribed (Mithric) "varumani".
			* “that is, trolls” has been scratched on the slate next to it (Archontean).
		* 47 cp; 56 sp; 41 gp; a 75 gp gem

8 huge spiders: SZ M; AL N; AC 6; MV 180’; HD 2+2; HP 18, 15, 15, 14, 13, 12, 11, 10; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: surprise 1-5; poison (+1 to saves); can leap up to 30’.

6 / 15
### 4-157: Carved Chamber

* Every inch of the walls and ceiling of this rounded chamber has been carved with 1”-deep geometric and representational figures.
	* The figures are hard to make out, bodies elongated and twisted, but the following are clear: thin-limbed bipeds (rudishva), bird-men (varuda), long- and heavy-limbed bipeds (varumani), and snake-men (kaliyani).
		* The faces have all been systematically obliterated with destructive magic, and three sections of carving that carried inscriptions have been utterly obliterated.
	* A 5’-square chunk of the east wall has been completely removed.
* The passage north ends in a cave-in.  A tiny, cramped tunnel continues wending upward, ending at one of the cells in the prison of Set (3-105d).
* Secret Door (south): opened by pushing a 3”-tall image of a door on the section of the western wall of 4-157 closest to the entrance.
* The chamber was built by the rudishva to tell the story of the Beacon and its inhabitants.
	* The priest of Thoth who discovered the chamber destroyed the wall images but carted off a section featuring an enormous image of the Beacon (see 4-158).
* The chamber is peaceful, quiet and secure, and would make a good refuge.

### 4-158: Secret Chamber

* The chamber has the same carved walls and rounded corners as 4-157.
	* A dangerous invisible field of magical energy bisects the chamber at a point 8’ from the southern wall.
		* After several millennia, however, the trap is malfunctioning.
			* Every 3d6 rounds it shimmers briefly into visibility.
			* A non-rudishva organism touching or crossing is zapped (6d6, save vs breath weapons for 3/4 damage).  Only 1d6 discharges left before it fails.
	* The northern secret door can only be opened as described in 4-157.
	* A chest of gray plasteel lies against the south wall.
		* The chest is empty, robbed in antiquity by whoever dug the tunnel to the east.
		* The chest holds the projector module for the field (2 zaps left).
	* Lying in the center of the room is a desiccated corpse in the orange robes of a Thothian priest, charred by energy or electricity.
		* 15 ancient silver pennies, key to the left hematite door (3-177), and an eye of seeing (new).
		* Floating next to the body is a 5’ x 5’ x 1’ segment of stone (4200 lbs) covered with strange carvings (the piece taken from the wall in 4-157). 
			* The slab rests on a permanent enhanced floating disk of the priest’s devising (responds to command words (Mithric): “Go!”, “Stop!”, etc. 
			* The slab (1000-4000 gp to a Collegia or imperial scholars) depicts a strange dwelling shaped like a flattened sphere, standing on six piers, with numerous ‘antennae’ protruding from it. A ramp descends form the body of the dwelling to the ground, and numerous representatives of the four races depicted in 4-157 are shown on the ramp. Beneath the carving is the phrase, in Rudishva glyphis, “Shining Beacon of Glorious Heaven.”

### 4-159: Stairs Up to 3-212a

* These stairs climb to 3-212a.
	* They are used by the cult of Set to visit the upper levels of the dungeon.
	* A bright yellow arrow floats a foot above the ground, pointing up the stairs.
* Secret Door (north): hard to locate (1 in 8), opens by sliding an extremely thin pin (pick, etc; 1/8” thick) along the crack between the door and the floor.
	* It leads via a dusty staircase and natural tunnel to 4-158.

### 4-160: Crossroads

* An important crossroads for moving about the middle levels of the dungeon.
	* Relatively clear of debris and dust.
	* Each time the party enters, roll on the following table:
		* If the party comes from the west (4-163), any encounter here is warned of their approach by the booming of the magic mouth, won't be surprised, and has  an additional chance to surprise (3-in-6).

### 4-161: Long tunnel to 6-67

* This corridor descends 350’ over a quarter mile before ending up at the Arena (6-67). 

### 4-162: Hall of the Set Animals, w/ access to SL8-19

* This 15’-tall octagonal hall has a pretty vaulted ceiling, and much faded, but still visible artwork whose effect is busy, garish, and slightly chaotic.
	* South wall: a huge (10’ x 15’) fresco of a Set animal’s head.
	* Other walls: Set animals in various poses – standing, jumping, attacking, climbing walls, climbing trees, etc.
	* Secret Door (south): opens by pressing the painted eye of a specific Set animal.
		* Leads to a staircase descending 200’ to the long forgotten Set animal breeding caves of SL8-19. 
		* The modern Set cult is unaware of the secret door.

### 4-163: Many Stairs and Loud Voice

* Three important staircases meet at this landing.
* A magic mouth by the eastern stairs, speaks if movement occurs within 10’.
	* It emits five extremely loud, booming bass tones (wordless), which echo up the northern and eastern stairs.
	* The mouth resets after one hour, ready to echo again. 

### 4-164: Hall of the Worthies

* The door to this chamber is stuck in a partly open position.
* Within is an impressive hall 30’ tall and adorned with ancient veined-marble pavers and sheathing.
	* Three hemispherical marble plinths (5’ high) line each of the east and west walls, each (except A) is occupied by a statue.
		* Each is a statue of one of the Twenty Worthies of the Archontean Empire, their name incised across its plinth.
	*  A 3’-wide and 8’-deep basin, filled with a murky, sludgy liquid, runs the length of the room between two rows of three rectangular granite platforms (3’ tall), one in front of each plinth.
	* The south wall has been damaged by some tunneling creature, with a 3’ hole broken through 15’ off the ground.
	* A massive mosaic spans the entire south wall.
		* In the center, in 5’-tall script (Mithric) “Let the Worthy Illuminate the [gap].”
			* The gap where they tunnel emerges contained the word “Unworthy” (may find the fragments in the rubble below the hole.
		* Below the inscription is an image of a robed human standing on a platform looking at a statue of a warrior.
		* To the sides of the inscription are colossal images (same socialist-realist mode of the colossi on the cliff face) of Arden and Vul, the former leaning on her spear while gazing impassively at the inscription, and the latter, face obscured by hood, pointing to the inscription with a wand.

The Statues
* In ancient days these legendary heroes were archetypes of behavior and profession, and might still be familiar to more bookish PCs.
* A statue's magic is activated when a person stands on a platform, faced the appropriate worthy, and declaims “Let the Worthy Illuminate the Unworthy.”
	* A bit more dangerous in the present day, due to magical decay.
		* If the phrase is mangled or not spoken within a minute, a negative effect is produced from the basin behind the postulant.
		* In a few cases, the magic is malfunctioning.
	* The magic of each statue will only work once per person.

* A. Priscus Pulcher, the Arch-Sortian
	* The name has been badly damaged, but is still just legible
	* Statue: completely missing.  A wreath of fragrant and fresh flowers rests on the plinth (replaced every 2-8 days).
		* A Priscian mage?
	* Magical Effect: none
	* Negative Effect: none

* B. Licinia the Seer
	* Statue: a heavy-set woman in a toga with arms at her side. Her eyes are exaggeratedly large and empty.
	* Magical Effect: Licinia represents power over/in the future. She intones the following phrase in affectless Mithric: ‘Our eyes see deeds that are yet to be; to unlock those sights ask thy questions three.’ The postulant can then ask up to three questions about the future. 
		* The GM should provide truthful answers, although he/she will have to be more speculative about contingent events.
	* Negative Effect: the liquid in the basin turns slightly gelatinous and rises as a tentacle from the basin. The postulant on the platform is struck by the liquid (no save) and is cursed such that he/she will be -2 to all die rolls for the next month. This curse will not be immediately evident, of course.

* C. Thrygga the Mighty
	* Statue: a warrior clad in ancient imperial field plate, with two hands clutching a massive claymore.
		* The statue’s head is missing; a fountain of colored sparks spews continuously from its truncated neck.
			* The sparks rain down in a 5’ radius (they burn for 3d4 and produce a lasting, and brightly colored, scar, on the hand/arm (50%) or face (50%).
	* Magical Effect: the positive effect is malfunctioning, and anyone who steps on the platform - regardless of what he/she utters - will activate the negative effect.
	* Negative Effect: the liquid in the basin boils and, after 3 rounds, a cloudkill spell is activated. It takes 2 rounds to fill the chamber.

* D. Plotinus Quartus Claudino, Archon
	* Statue: a dignified man, dressed in a toga and wearing an olive wreath. A set of fasces is cradled in one arm, other is raised in greeting (three fingers, palm outward). 
	* Magical Effect: Plotinus represents power in the present. He responds in the measured tones of a practiced orator: My writ runs over all that I now see; for knowledge of the same ask thy questions three. Plotinus answers questions about current events, individuals, and locations; he does so elliptically, but at some length.
	* Negative Effect: the liquid in the basin roils and bubbles; after 1 round an exact duplicates of all visitors clamber forth and confront the originals. These duplicates have the same statistics and equipment as the PCs, if defeated they melt into sludgy liquid. The duplicates cannot cast spells, but are able to mimic magic items.

* E. Yeth, Who Sought to Bring Law to Chaos
	* Statue: a gnarled, bent man dressed in rags, with wild, unkempt hair. He carries no objects, and his arms are splayed in a wild manner. His eyes bug wildly.
	* Magical Effect: Yeth represents chaos and randomness. He wildly screeches a series of unrhymed nonsense: Blue rills of ethereal bone drip upward to the globular leaves of prophecy!
		* Roll 1d20-2 on the chart below.
	* Negative Effect: the liquid in the basin roils for a round and then explodes in a wet, gooey mess over the room. Roll 1d20+2 on the chart below.

Modified d20 Effect
* -1 to 0 One random attribute is permanently raised by 1
* 1-2 Vigor: PC gains 4-6 HP permanently
* 3-4 Infravision granted to PC; duration is either one month (75%) or permanent (25%)
* 5-6 Regenerate: for one day, PC regenerates 1 HP per round
* 7-8 Stone Sight: see 30’ through stone for 1 day
* 9-10 Cure: heal 3-24 hp; if at full hp, excess becomes tHP
* 11-12 Sex change, permanent
* 13-14 Animal attraction: chance for wandering monsters increases for month
* 15-16 Bleeder: 5+ damage from a single blow causes bleeding of 1 HP/hr.  5+ HP magic healing delays bleeding 1d4 hours, only heal or remove curse permanently removes it.
* 17-18 Frenzied: 25% chance to go berserk in combat (duration 1 month): +1-6 HP, +1 to hit, -2 to AC, 25% chance to attack comrades once foes are defeated
* 19-20 Geas to find the death mask of Ptoh-Ristus (3-66)
* 21-22 One random attribute is permanently lowered by 1

* F. Horatius Interfector, Sorcerer
	* Statue: A wiry man dressed in tunic, sandals, and a strange open-faced helmet. He carries a skull in one hand and a human femur in the other.
	* Magical Effect: Horatius represents power over the past. He snaps the following, in Mithric: Deeds of the dead are known to me; of those that were, ask your questions three. The PCs can then ask up to three questions about the past. Horatius answers questions directly, but economically.
	* Negative Effect: the liquid in the basin roils unsettlingly, before a number of undead crabs (2 per party member) clamber from the basin to assault the intruder(s)
		* SZ M; AL N; AC 4; MV 90’; HD 3; HP 20, 18; #AT 2; Dmg 2-8/2-8; MR 25%. Special defenses: half damage from piercing weapons; turned as spectres

### 4-165: Tunnel to SL5-1

* This long tunnel snakes through the earth and rock, damp and slippery with mud, descending 75’ to the lizardman caves (SL5-1).
	* The lizardmen have dug 3 pit traps covered with a screens of reeds and mud.
		* The pits are 20' deep, with filth-smeared wooden stakes (2d6 falling, 1d6 stakes, 2-in-6 chance of disease).

## Level 4: 166 - 180

### 4-166: Wet Cavern

* This cavern is damp and dripping. Two deep pools of fresh water occupy either side of the cave.
	* Clear humanoid tracks lead to the north (lizardman).
	* A spear is lodged in the rock next to the opening of the north passage, topped with a human skull spiked with primitive darts.
	* The southern passage is narrow, rocky, and twisty, debouching 30’ above the floor of 4-181.
		* Obvious and fresh bloodstains dot this passageway, left by Gillen and his gang (4-180) dragging corpses to 4-181.

### 4-167: Blue Pillar

* This ancient chamber has a ruined dome of light-blue tiles, supported by a 25’-tall hexagonal pillar (5’ per side) of blue marble.
	* The floor is littered with broken tiles and blue dust.
		* A clear path leads east to 4-163.
	* On each side of the pillar, at human head-height, is carved a bas-relief of a face.
		* First Face (northeast): A very handsome, youngish man with lively eyes, trim beard, and empty sockets where the eyes should be (an accurate portrait of Priscus Pulcher), now defaced (broken nose, worn features, and ancient graffiti (Mithric) “Betrayer!“).
			* Not the usual image of the Philosopher, but this is a Sortian face (new) and can be activated with Sortian eyes.  Unique combos:
				* Gold-Gold: Teleportation
					* All within 5’ are teleported to area 6-48
				* Gold-Sapphire: a magic mouth speaks (Mithric)
					* "They are sure to be watching the pillar, now that Priscus has been executed and the League dispersed. So much for the way of negotiation. Let Livia cajole. I, Macrinus, tell my fellow Sortians that we must arm ourselves! The Order and the Temples respect only strength. Perhaps a taste of their own medicine will make them more amenable to our demands."
					* GM Note: references the fate of Priscus Pulcher. Livia the Lictor and Macrinus Furiosus were other Sortian leaders who differed in approach; Livia favoring discussion and Macrinus warfare (see SL11-13 and SL11-15). Also refers to the Order of Thoth and the temples (of Thoth, Set and Horus), who opposed the Sortians.
		* Second Face (east): A dignified middle-aged woman with aquiline nose, pursed lips and narrowed eyes.
			* The pupils are sized to hold ancient gold solidi (1” diameter, 1/4” thick).
			* If two are inserted, the coins disappear and all within a 20’-long cone in front of the face are teleported to the antechamber to the audience chamber of the Governor’s Palace in the ruins of Arden Vul.
			* That room collapsed long ago; now users arrive 10' above the rubble pile at AV-29, falling for d6.  Surprised travelers have a nice aerial view of the palace, including the stump of the Obelisk of the Moon (AV-28).
		* Third Face (southeast): A monstrous face, with sharp cheekbones, pronounced supra-orbital bones, a thin, elongated nose, and unnatural eyes [a varumani].
			* The mouth is opened in a flattened oval, just big enough to hold one of the troll thegn’s passports (av items).
			* If a passport is placed in the mouth, all standing in a 20’-long cone before this face are teleported to 7-1 in the troll thegn’s domain.
		* Fourth Face (southwest): formerly a Set-animal, now almost obliterated.
			* Only the characteristic square ears of the animal remain.
		* Fifth Face (west): a long, narrow face of a man with a pronounced cranium, sharp chin, and crooked nose (a caricature of a priest of Thoth), wearing an ibis medallion.
			* The pupils of the face are small (1/2” in diameter), sized for ancient silver pennies.  If two are inserted, all in a 20’-long cone before the priest’s face are teleported to the Great Hall of Thoth (3-123).
		* Sixth Face (northwest): A wizened, goblin face with pointed ears and pointed teeth in its grinning mouth.
			* The nose is absent, leaving a 3”-diameter, 1’ deep hole.
			* Placing a gem (any value) in the hole teleports all in a cone before the face to the old workers’ quarters, now the goblin king’s court (SL4-53).
* This chamber is the destination for the Sortian face at 6-48. Arrivals find themselves standing at the south side of the room, facing the blue pillar.

### 4-168: Stairs Down to SL13-9

* These stairs descend 700’ through several direction changes to the checkpoint at SL13-9. 

### 4-169: Blocked Corridor

* The corridor here is completely blocked by a cave-in.

### 4-170: Entrance to the Precincts of Set

* This small room marks the southern boundary of the Set cult’s power.
	* Pilgrims can rest before the long trek up the stairs to the red bridge (4-120a) and the Forum (4-2).
	* Two 10’-tall portable ‘statues’ of Set stand on either side of the stairway.
		* They are made of wood and plaster, and are painted brightly.  Cave moisture has rendered them moldy, and the pain is beginning to run.
		* One statue is of a man with bone-white face and bright red hair; the other has a human body but Set-Animal head.
	* The chamber is lit by continual lights placed on the heads of the statues.
* Note: if the submerged door at AV-39 was recently opened (within a few days or so) and the southern swamp drained, both statues are gone and the chamber is marked by signs of a massive flow of water. The Set cult will replace the statues within 1-4 months.

##### 4-170a: Supplies

* The Set cult stores some supplies in this ruined corridor segment, behind a wall of force.
	* The shimmering wall is impervious to assault, but lowers for 1 Turn if touched with any Set was stick (new).
* Inside are substantial digging supplies (picks, hammers, shovels, sacks), rope and pulleys for EX-15; a spare basket for EX-15, and three crates of weapons marked with the imperial seal.

### 4-171: Ancient Hall

* The stairs from 4-177 lead out of the water into a large, brightly lit, dry chamber.
	* The ceiling rises 35’ above the floor.
	* The southern entrance is 25’ up the south wall; the north door is at floor level.
		* Directly below the south entrance is a Thothian teleportation ring (BK-RE-BL-GR-YE-WH). No glass activation squares are present.
		* The north door once led to an important suite, but the corridor has collapsed.
	* A platform at the same level of the south entrance stands 15’ inside the room.
		* A narrow stair leads down from this first platform to a second platform, from which two staircases reach the floor.  Both platforms are carved from a single block of stone.
	* The walls are impressively decorated with bas-reliefs depicting the first and third mysteries of Set on the western and eastern walls (see 4-23 and 4-111)
	* Four 25’ statues of Set in Set animal form flanking both entrances.
		* Each statue features fist-sized blue quartz eyes (250 gp each) (there are no negative effects to removing these eyes).
* Numerous corpses dot the floor of the chamber.
	* One corpses carries a scroll with 200 year-old adventuring notes.
	* A token of Arden (av items); chain mail +2; hammer +2; an enchanted spear named   Treefeller (new); a scroll (garrulous mouth (new), stinking cloud, gust of wind, cloudkill); a scroll (lightning bolt, fire shield); 34 gp; 56 sp, a bundle of adventuring notes.
* From the south entrance shapes can be seen moving around on the floor of the chamber. 
	* These are shadows under the control of the spectre.
	* The spectre lurks on the second, lower platform, hoping to surprise anyone who leaps from the entrance corridor to the higher platform.

Adventuring Notes (approximately 200 years old)
* The lost tagma is dominated by a witch they call Deino; she is performing foul sorcery on them such that they no longer appear as legionaries.  They have occupied the old administrative center of the priesthood of Thoth. Whipped on by her spells, they took Gaius and Theodoric.
* We fled to the great cavern, where Ptarmis’s great work has reverted to savagery.  There we lost our minions to the fungal people.
* We finally fled to the west, and down a set of long stairs.  We spent [hole in manuscript] at the thegn’s court, where we rested before attempting to find the old exit of Set.
* GM Note: refers to the beastmen of Level 3 (3-123 to 3-162) and to Deino (3-158), evidence for the transformation of the lost tagma into beastmen.  References the great cavern (3-163 and 3-172) and the fungal foresters that inhabit it, and finally to the troll thegn’s court (7-75).

6 shadows: SZ M; AL CE; AC 7; MV 120; HD 3+3; HP 24, 21, 20, 20, 19, 17; #AT 1; Dmg 2-5. Special attacks: STR drain. Special defenses: 90% undetectable; +1 or better weapons to hit; immune to sleep, charm, hold, and cold. 

1 spectre: SZ M; AL LE; AC 2; MV 150’, 300’ flying (Class B); HD 7+3; HP 52; #AT 1; Dmg 1-8. Special attacks: energy drain. Special defenses: +1 or better weapons to hit; immune to sleep, charm, hold, cold, poison, and paralysis.

X / 52
### 4-172: Cave of Lost Colossi

* A strong breeze blows from north to south through this flattened, sandy cave. 
	* Moisture drips from the walls (the Set cult keeps the area sanded, so the floor is only damp).
		* Booted tracks lead to the north.
	* 3 smooth granite heads (10’ tall) with stylized generic features rest at crazy angles in the sand.
		* The pupils of each are missing.
		* The cave moisture has caused numerous runnels of water to stain their faces.
	* The tunnel north is broad and even; east is rocky and difficult.

* Note: If the submerged door at AV-39 was recently opened, draining the southern swamp, the sand is gone and the three colossal heads are piled up against the southern entrance.  Signs of the passage of a large volume of muddy water will be evident.
	* Passage between 4-172 and 4-178 will be impossible for 4-7 days, until the Set cult levers the heads out of the way.

### 4-173: Caves

* This area is uneven and dangerous due to the moisture that covers all the rock surfaces.
	* Numerous beautiful flowstone formations and stalactites dot the area.
	* Halfway up the northern protrusion is the encrusted body of a priest of Set, who died here after his leg was fractured.
		* It would be easy to miss the skeleton unless one clambered all the way to the end of the protrusion.
		* Near the body are a broken deacon’s was stick (new), an ebony wand of trap and secret door detection (16 charges), and a silk purse (2 huge rhodochrosite gems, shaped like eyes for one of the colossi in 4-172, 2500 gp each).
	* The southern tunnel is quite narrow, appearing as if it will peter out, but it continues to the fissure (4-174).

### 4-174: Fissure

* This fissure is not particularly wide, but extends 75’ below and 50’ above the level of the two entrances.
	* The walls are craggy and slick with moisture.
	* The entrance tunnels cannot be seen from one another without actually entering the fissure.
	* A pod of chasm cephalopods lives here; very hungry from lack of traffic.

6 small chasm cephalopods (see new monsters): SZ S; AL N; AC 5; MV 60’ flying (Class A); HD 2; HP 14, 13, 13, 12, 11, 8; #AT 5 (4 tentacles and a beak); Dmg 1-3/1-3/1-3/1-3/1-4; MR 25%. Special attacks: surprise on 1-4.

### 4-175: Wet Cave

* This cave is damp, with numerous stalactites of all sizes.

##### 4-175a: Tunnel Down to SL12-13

* The northern tip of 4-175 turns into a 4’-diameter, natural tunnel.
	* It slopes upward through multiple curves, until reaching SL12-13. 

### 4-176: Pitiful Scene

* Small stalactites line the ceiling, and dripping water sounds throughout the cavern.
	* Two 2’-tall, doll-like figures huddle by a small light in the center of this long cave.
		* They huddle around a 3” tall magical light emitter shedding light in a 15’ circle.  One is motionless, while the other sobs and weeps over its companion.
		* The dolls are two of Kerbog Khan’s automatons.  A piercer crushed one fatally.  The other, with a surprising degree of sentience, is mourning its companion.

Cheren (Corbel)
Checheg (Cobban)

* The ‘living’ automaton, Cheren (Corbel), is made of wood, metal strips, and bone.
	* She is dressed in the simple clothes of a female peasant.
	* Cheren is distraught that her friend, Checheg, has been rendered ‘inoperative.’
		* She is certain that Kerbog Khan will not accord him a burial, and will render aid to any who bury Checheg with dignity.
			* Should explorers comply, Cheren accompanies them for two weeks.
		* Checheg is a masterpiece of automaton and would sell to a wizard or magical collegium for a substantial sum, which would completely alienate Cheren.

Cheren
* Cheren can walk at a 15' speed, or will ride in a backpack.
* She chatters the entire time, with a sharp tongue, offering a running critique of her carrier’s actions.
* She knows accurate information of her route from Kerbog Khan’s workshops to Level 4 (they fled from SL12-13 to 4-175a, and then to this location).
* She places the magical light in her chest cavity for transport.

Kerbog Khan
* Checheg build a small talisman that blocks Kerbog's ability to track / control automatons within 10' of it.  It's on his body.  Cheren doesn't realize its significance, and will leave it behind, making her visible to Kerbog again.
* Kerbog Khan may attempt to seize control of Cheren’s brain and eyes (10% cumulative chance per encounter).
	* Her eyes will glow bright yellow and a deep, masculine voice echoes from her.
	* Kerbog Khan’s ability to control his automatons declines with distance, so Cheren would be relatively safe if taken outside of Arden Vul.
	* To fully release her from Kerbog Khan’s control would take a sage and several spells. 
* Kerbog Khan first negotiates and then, if necessary, casts spells through her.
	* He interprets ‘necessary’ as any circumstance in which Cheren’s new friends attempt to prevent Cheren from doing his direct bidding.
	* Immobilizing her limbs and physically holding her mouth closed, can prevent Kerbog Khan from interacting by speech or spell.

8 piercers: SZ M(x4) and S(x4); AL N; AC 3; MV 10’; HD 3(x4) and 2(x4); HP 22, 19, 18, 15, 14, 13, 11, 9; #AT 1; Dmg 3-18 (x4) and 2-12(x4). Special attacks: 95% to surprise prey.

Cheren, one of the children automatons of Kerbog Khan (see new monsters): SZ S; AL NG; AC 6; MV 60’; HD 2; HP 13; #AT 1; Dmg 1-2; MR 20%. Special defenses: immune to cold.

### 4-177: Flooded Hall

* This ancient hall is flooded 10’ deep, with the ceiling another 10’ above the water.
	* The western wall collapsed centuries ago, leaving an impressive rock fall looming out of the water.
	* The southwestern tunnel enters the hall 10’ above the water line.
	* On the floor of the hall, under 10’ of water, is a heavy iron chest (75 lb).
		* It is trapped with explosive runes.
		* A rod of rulership (15 charges); Ritha Ferk, an enchanted battle axe (new), two ancient maps, and two 10-lb platinum bars (2,500 gp each).
			* The maps disintegrate if the chest is opened underwater.
* The waters are home to 6 water ghouls, who attack any swimmers.

6 lacedons: SZ M; AL CE; AC 6; MV 90’, 90’ swimming; HD 2; HP 15, 15, 13, 12, 10, 10; #AT 3; Dmg 1-3/1-3/1-6. Special attacks: paralysis. Special defenses: immune to sleep and charm.

### 4-178: Rocky Cave

* A steady breeze blows from the northwest to the south through this uneven, 20’-tall cave.
	* Two large standing boulders (10’ tall) bisect the cave.
		* The southern boulder is flat-topped (10’ long by 4’ wide); an abandoned cache of dungeoneering equipment atop it.
			* 10 spikes, two 11’ poles, two 50’ coils of rope, a bullseye lantern, 4 flasks of lantern oil, a packet of chalk, a dozen marbles in a leather pouch, and a scroll of cure serious wounds.
	* Subtle (2-in-6) bare footprints in the mud lead northeast (lizardmen).
	* (1 in 6) signs of struggle and bloodstains lead towards 4-179.

* Note: if the submerged door at AV-39 was recently opened (within a few days or so) and the southern swamp drained, the boulders are piled up against the southern entrance, the dungeoneering equipment is gone, and signs of the passage of a large volume of muddy water will be evident..
	* Passage to the south will be possible, but slow.
	* After 4-7 days, the Set Cult pushes the boulders back into the center of the chamber.

### 4-179: Ruined Hall

* A tall (30’), damp cave, with a large boulder in its middle.
	* Carved by water over the past millennium, leading to the collapse of what had been a major hall in antiquity.
	* Remnants of it and its connecting corridors are glimpsed throughout the room at various points.
		* West, 20’ up the cave wall, is a corridor fragment holding a nest of giant rats (they attack only if their nest is threatened).
		* East, 15’ up the cave wall, is another corridor fragment to a forgotten section of the main stair (4-180).
		* 3 tips of ancient columns project 2-4’ out of the rocky debris of the cave floor. 
	* Blood trails (1 in 6 to detect) lead both to 4-180 and 4-166.
	* Gillen and his gang (4-180) are content to observe PCs who pass through this cavern.
		* If the PCs investigate the entrance to 4-180, they will take aggressive action.

12 giant rats: SZ S; AL N(E); AC 7; MV 120’; HD 1-4 HP; HP 4(x3), 3(x3), 2(x3), 1(x3); #At 1; Dmg 1-3. Special attacks: 5% chance of disease.

### 4-180: Stair Remnant

* A party of evil adventurers led by Gillen the magic user has discovered this inaccessible, and dry, segment of the old main stairway.
	* From this base, they ambush visitors to the Forum (4-2), keeping any valuables and selling captives to the Guild of Service (see 4-11, 4-12 and 4-13).
	* They have 4 prisoners, bound in the southern bit of stairs.
* Tressa set a tripwire across the opening to 4-179.
	* It drops a large rock on the head of the first person through the entrance to 4-180.
	* Deals 1d6, may knocks the victim to the floor of 4-179 (another 1d6+3 damage).
* The fragment of the old staircase bears an unusual but lovely frieze of the second mystery of Set (4-48) (1000 gp if somehow removed and sold).
	* Images of a priest, circular room, the sandstorm, scorpions, and audience.

* The adventurers are cautious and careful.
	* They do not relish combat with equals, and are happy to negotiate if pressed.
	* They prefer to threaten from the (relative) security of their fastness (since PCs won’t know that it is a dead end).
* Two days ago the robbers ambushed a prosperous merchant and his guard in 4-178.
	* They are waiting for the right moment to sell the survivors.
* Gillen is aware that the Set cult will begin looking for the culprit(s) after a few more ambushes.
	* The gang will move on within 2 weeks when the PCs first encounter them.
	* Relocate them elsewhere in the upper Halls (maybe in Level 3 or SL-3).
* Cinna Minux, the vampire (7-122), has charmed Gillen, Tressa, and Quade; he occasionally pumps them for information about Level 4.
* The gang's loot
	* 849 cp, 707 sp, and 846 gp; one large carpet (175 gp, but heavy); two casks of fine brandy (60 gp each); and three lion pelts (75 gp each).
		* One pelt is actually a lion cloak (new).
	* Mogret’s trade goods: 6 heavy packs loaded with flour (x3), dried beans (x1), yeast (x1), and root vegetables (x1) (100 gp/pack in the Forum of Set).

Gillen, 5th-level male Archontean magic user: SZ M; AL CE; AC 8; MV 120’; HD 5; HP 18; #AT 1; Dmg staff (1-6). Abilities: STR 9, INT 16, WIS 14, DEX 16, CON 15, CHA 14. 
* Possessions: staff; wand of magic missiles (28 charges); potion of extra healing; potion of levitation; a scroll with Frigg’s flatulence and Frigg’s caustic kisses (see new spells for both). 
* Spells memorized: charm person, magic missile, shield, sleep; invisibility, web; fireball. 

Gordy, 3rd-level male Archontean fighter: SZ M; AL LN; AC 5; MV 90’; HD 3; HP 30; #AT 1; Dmg 3-10 (battle axe +1). Abilities: STR 17, INT 8, WIS 10, DEX 15, CON 17, CHA 8. 
* Possessions: ring mail and shield; battle axe +1; potion of diminution; a rope of climbing.

Quade, 2nd-level female Archontean fighter: SZ M; AL N; AC 4; MV 90’; HD 2; HP 19; #AT 1; Dmg 2-9 (long sword), 1-4 (light crossbow). Abilities: STR 16, INT 9, WIS 10, DEX 13, CON 18,

Prisoners

Mogret of Narsileon, male Thorcin merchant (prisoner): SZ M; AL LE; AC 10; MV 120’; HD 1-1; HP 4; #AT 1; Dmg by weapon.
* Mogret is a merchant but also a spy for the imperial Drome (see World of Archontos appendix).  If released and escorted either to Newmarket or to the Forum (4-2), he will provide a written testimonial entitling the holder to a reward of 500 gp from the Prosperity Factor in Narsileon.
	* He's was on the way to look for Callista, who had stopped reporting.

Ulf the Dim, 2nd-level male Wiskin fighter (prisoner): SZ M; AL NE; AC 10; MV 120’; HD 2; HP 17; #AT 1; Dmg by weapon. Abilities: STR 17, INT 7, WIS 8, DEX 14, CON 16, CHA 13. 
* Ulf was one of Mogret’s bodyguards, and is possible henchman fodder. He is stupid and mean.

Stylesia, 3rd-level female Archontean fighter (prisoner): SZ M; AL LN; AC 9; MV 120’; HD 3; HP 27; #AT 1; Dmg by weapon. Abilities: STR 16, INT 7, WIS 10, DEX 15, CON 16, CHA 9.
* She was also one of Mogret’s bodyguard. She is smart and loyal, but afraid of insects.

Bestor, male Archontean messenger (prisoner): SZ M; AL NG; AC 10; MV 120’; HD 1-1; HP 5; #AT 1; Dmg by weapon.
* Bestor is a messenger from Lord Burdock (see World of Archontos appendix).
* He appears weaselly and weak, and the Guild of Service declined to purchase him from Gillen.  The robbers are stymied, and trying to decide what to do with him.
* Lord Burdock might redeem him for 200 gp.
* Bestor is tougher and more loyal than he looks, for he has successfully concealed the message in his anus.
* Ironically, the message contains a secret offer of alliance between Lord Burdock and High Priestess Stephania.
* That information would be politically damaging to Lord Burdock; it could be sold to him for 5,000 gp or to Keko the Lame in Narsileon for 7,500 gp (see World of Archontos appendix).
* Bestor did not recognize the Guild of Service, which is why he did not explain his mission to them; he was told to speak only to the high priestess.

Gillen’s spell book: burning hands, charm person, dancing lights, detect magic, Frigg’s flatulence (see new spells), friends, magic missile, read magic, sleep, spider climb; darkness 15’ radius, detect invisibility, false trap, Frigg’s caustic kisses (see new spells), mirror image, stinking cloud, web; fireball, hold person, protection from normal missiles, water breathing. 

## Level 4: 181 - 190

### 4-181: Stalactite and Stalagmite Cave

* This large chamber is formed by the fusion of one of the ancient halls with some new cave formations. 
	* There are finished sections west, north and south, with smoothed walls and floors. 
		* The northernmost wall has a section of living mosaic (new) depicting the Red Bridge of Set (4-120a); 25% chance some sort of activity is going on there. 
	* The chamber center and three entrances are natural caverns from subsequent geological activity, their floors rocky and covered with debris.
	* The area is damp, the walls coated with the light-purple fungus common to this area (see 4-184).
	* Dozens of stalactites and stalagmites have formed in the center and north. 
		* Most are slender, with four pillar-sized stalagmites amid the smaller ones.
			* An ancient roper, lurks among these large stalagmites, feeding on beetles and other vermin, but hoping for better prey.
	* The bodies of 3 dead mercenaries (part of Mogret’s guard, see 4-180) have been dumped from the passage to the north (the roper has only partially devoured them).

1 roper: SZ L; AL CE; AC 0; MV 30’; HD 11; HP 80; #AT 1; Dmg 5-20; MR 80%. Special attacks: six poisonous strands (20’-50’ range; reduce STR by 50% in 1-3 rds). Special defenses: immune to lightning; take half damage from cold.
* In the roper’s gut: 7 ancient octagonal platinum coins; 8 gems (10-1,000 gp each); and a ring of spider climbing (new).

X / 80
### 4-182: Pool

* This wide spot in the tunnel network contains a broad pool of fresh water, frequented by most of the local monstrous denizens. 
* The entire area is covered with the crackly light-purple fungus (for effects see 4-184). 

### 4-183: Stair Fragment

* Amid the light-purple fungus (for effects, see 4-184) ubiquitous to these regions stands this fragment of the ancient stairway to Set.
	* A recent minor cave-in has revealed the corpse of an elite guardsmen of Arden Vul, dead over 1,400 years. 
		* The guardsman wears a suit of imperial field plate +2 (av items, needs 100 gp of repairs by a skilled armorer).
			* It will inevitably draw attention from the envious and suspicious; wearing it near imperial officials will lead to arrest, while the greedy will attempt to relieve the wearer of it.

### 4-184: Cave with Spiders

* This wide spot in the tunnels is slightly drier than the others.
	* A pack of huge spiders lairs here, their webs and nest in the northwestern extension.
		* Amid the webs are the husks of three lizardmen, two Set guardsmen, and a human magic user.
			* A lizardman sacred stone idol (see SL5-15); 18 sp; 23 gp; a suit of Set armor (av items); a short sword, a fragment of a letter, the mage's spellbook.
	* The walls, floors, and ceilings of this cave and the surrounding tunnels are covered with a light purple fungus that crackles slightly when trodden upon.
		* It is slippery (3d6 under DEX or -1 to attack), and stealth almost impossible.

8 huge spiders: SZ M; AL N; AC 6; MV 180’; HD 2+2; HP 18, 15, 15, 14, 13, 12, 11, 10; #AT 1; Dmg 1-6. Special attacks: surprise 1-5; poison (+1 to saves); can leap up to 30’.

Letter
* (Mithric and then Archontean translation) "Although he loved nothing more than the mundane work of stone carving and preparing the dead, the greatness of Theskelon could not be denied … after his demise, his followers prepared a resting spot hidden from view but close at hand.”
* A second hand adds (Archontean) “The tomb lies to the east of the southern necropolis.”
* GM Note: This letter refers to the tomb of the famous Theskelon (4-142).

Dead mage’s spell book: alarm, comprehend languages, dancing lights, enlarge, feather fall, identify, jump, magic aura, protection from evil, read magic, sleep, wizard mark; audible glamer, deeppockets, detect evil, forget, invisibility, irritation, levitate, rope trick, wizard lock, zephyr, and locate place (see new spells).

### 4-185: Stair Fragment

* This area of corridor leads to a mostly-collapsed section of the old main stair.
	* It is inaccessible to the golems in 4-187, but not to the beetles of the area.

### 4-186: Fungus and Beetle Cave

* This large, flat cave is covered by the ubiquitous, light-purple fungus in this section of the Halls (see 4-184).
	* The fungus has drawn a sizable colony of boring beetles (15 total, 8 here at a time).
		* Subtract random encounter casualties from this number; the beetles will replace 50% of their number within two weeks. 
		* They are ravenous and swarm their prey (no penalties as they crawl over each other to reach their targets)
	* In the northern section of the cave a sinkhole has opened a hole to one of the lost entrance halls.
		* The hole descends 5’ before opening into the ceiling of 4-187 (the floor of is another 30’ below).  Over time this hole will slowly increase in size.

8 giant boring beetles: SZ L; AL N; AC 3; MV 60’; HD 5; HP 38, 36, 33, 31, 30, 25, 23, 19; #AT 1; Dmg 5-20.

### 4-187: Ancient, Partly-Ruined Hall

* Once a sumptuous meeting halls near the entrance to the complex of Set, this chamber has been newly uncovered thanks to the sinkhole in 4-186.
	* The northern, eastern, and western walls are still in good condition, but the southeast corner has collapsed.
	* The area has succumbed to the light-purple fungus (see 4-184).
		* 4 boring beetles feed on the fungus.  They attack if the fungus is damaged.
	* A solid gold audience chair (15,000 gp, 300 lbs) sites on a marble dais to the west.
		* Nearby are the scattered bones of a long-dead human mage.
			* Among his bones and tatters: 3 gems (250 gp); a robe of useful items; a headband of intellect; a handy haversack (450 ancient silver pennies); and a Theodorus’ chair of great ease (new), and his spellbook.
		* Behind the dais stand two gruesome and rotting flesh golems (the mage's creations).
			* He ordered them to prevent all from seizing the chair, which he discovered shortly after the collapse of order in Arden Vul.  When he sat down to admire his treasure, the golems followed his poorly worded orders, went berserk, and ripped him apart. 
			* They still follow his instructions, and attack any who approach the dais.

2 flesh golems: SZ L; AL N; AC 9; MV 80’; HD 9, HP 40, 40; #AT 2; Dmg 2-16/2-16. Special defenses: +1 or better weapons to hit; immune to most spells, although fire and cold spells slow them.

4 giant boring beetles: SZ L; AL N; AC 3; MV 60’; HD 5; HP 36, 33, 30, 25; #AT 1; Dmg 5-20.

X / 36
X / 33
X / 30
X / 25

Spell book (badly damaged, but some spells remain): armor, shield, ventriloquism; pummeling fists of Arak-Zhorr (new), scare, wizard lock; harnessing the chaos (new); and Pol’s recall (new).

### 4-188: Battle Cave

* This damp cave holds the decomposing husks of three huge spiders and one giant boring beetle.
* The creatures were drawn here by the light purple fungus that coats these caves (for effects see 4-184) and slew each other.

### 4-189: Warning Cave

* A fairly strong breeze blows from the north through this large cave towards 4-190.
* Two mostly-skeletonized adventurers have been spiked to the north wall, spread-eagled.
	* They wear rags of clothing, but carry no equipment.
	* They are animated by the priests of Set.  If they perceive motion, the rotting skulls chatter out in unison (Archontean): “Lord Set watches his districts with care. Depart, ye unbelievers, lest he smite you in his wrath!”
* The knob-like rock protrusion on the south wall is a natural basin filled with clear water.
* The narrow opening (4’ wide) of the tunnel to the east is difficult to spot.

* Note: if the submerged door at AV-39 has been recently opened, draining the southern portion of the swamp, signs of the passage of a large volume of muddy water will be evident, and the animated skeletons will be gone. 

### 4-190: Exit to Cliff Face (EX-15)

* The cave exits the cliff face 650’ above the valley floor, or 850’ below the plateau.
	* The Set cult has a pulley system attached to an iron bar which can swing out into the air to raise and lower a wicker basket big enough for two humans with gear, attached a set of thick ropes .
	* When not in use, the basket, ropes, and pulleys are stored inside the entrance.
	* There is also a stone chest holding spikes, hammers, ropes, and a signal lantern with crimson panes.

* Note: if the submerged door at AV-39 has been recently opened, fraining the southern portion of the swamp, then the equipment, pulley, and basket will be gone.
	* Signs of the passage of a large volume of muddy water will be evident.
	* Until the Set cult has repaired the damage (after 3-7 days), there will be no easy egress from this cave to the valley floor.

* The mountain lion (EX-14) may take an interest in those investigating this area.
* Roll to see if any other creatures are currently using the cave entrance:
